Current Commentary

Desires for the North China Political Affairs Committee

Recently, the central government, recognizing the urgency of the situation in North China, and the need for strong leadership in military planning and maintaining order, has established the North China Political Affairs Committee as the highest authority responsible for planning and coordination to achieve effective response. Now, Chairman Huang Fu is about to go north to take office. The important mission of the North China Political Affairs Committee is about to begin. We cannot help but offer a few words of encouragement to the North China Political Affairs Committee.

The recent perilous situation in North China is almost as precarious as a swallow's nest on a curtain. The enemy army has already seized Jehol and is advancing southward with thunderous force. Their ambition is clear to all. At this time, the North is relying on a small number of battle-weary troops to resist the strong enemy and protect Tianjin. However, the enemy possesses powerful weapons and is moving a large army, sweeping across the land like a storm. Twenty days ago, Miyun, only about a hundred miles from Peiping, had already been bombed, and today enemy planes have been sighted in the skies over Peiping. The perilous situation in Peiping is foreseeable. If Peiping is lost, all of North China will be gone. Thinking of this, we cannot help but feel grief, anger, and sorrow. The North China Political Affairs Committee is being established precisely at this moment to shoulder this critical situation. Therefore, it is of utmost importance to strengthen unity and mobilize all forces to deal with it. This is the first point.

Recently, the enemy army has been attacking and seizing our key passes along the Great Wall. At the same time, they are using money to buy off a large number of shameless and degenerate vagrants and politicians to infiltrate Peiping and Tianjin, plotting to respond from within. Zhang Jingyao, who was recently killed by patriotic youth in Peiping at the Six Nations Hotel, is one example. However, this was only fortunately discovered by our patriotic youth in Peiping. There must still be many others who have been bought off by the enemy, lurking in various parts of North China, willing to act as accomplices, and who have not yet been discovered. Such conscienceless individuals are the public enemies of our nation. In maintaining the overall situation in North China, the North China Political Affairs Committee should pay close attention to this point, ensuring that these ugly characters have no place to stand and that their conspiracies are thwarted, in order to protect the tranquility of the rear. This is the second point.

Zhang Xueliang's failure was due to his consistent lack of resistance, losing territory and disgracing the nation, and was therefore abandoned by the people. Now that the North China Political Affairs Committee has been established, it must focus on military affairs in addition to politics, seeking to be different from Zhang Xueliang. In other words, those who previously did not resist must now actively resist, and only then can they live up to the heavy trust of the country and the ardent expectations of the people. This is the third point.

The situation is urgent! The situation is perilous! The fate of North China today hangs by a thread. Our North China Political Affairs Committee has been appointed to this critical mission. How will it work diligently and wholeheartedly to maintain it, so that Peiping and Tianjin do not become a continuation of Liaoning, Jilin, Heilongjiang, and Jehol, and extend the life of the nation by even a slim chance? This difficult and weighty responsibility now rests on the shoulders of the gentlemen of the North China Political Affairs Committee. May they remember it.

Confirmed Sale of the Chinese Eastern Railway

Soviet Russia Tries to Avoid Conflict with Japan

Strange words from Litvinov!

Claiming the Chinese government has failed to fulfill its obligations for eighteen months.

Believing it has lost the moral rights contained in the agreement.

(Moscow) Soviet Foreign Commissar Litvinov mentioned today China's request to be consulted on the Soviet-“Manchukuo” Chinese Eastern Railway dispute. According to Soviet semi-official news agency reports, Litvinov said that the Nanjing government or those in power under its control have ceased to be real partners with the Soviet Union regarding the Chinese Eastern Railway. According to the Peiping-Shenyang Agreement, the Chinese government must send representatives to attend the Railway Bureau. However, in the past eighteen months, the Chinese government has not sent a representative, so it has lost its moral rights contained in the agreement. Litvinov then mentioned the Sino-Soviet dispute in 1929, saying that the Russian government, in order to eliminate the cause of the conflict, had negotiated with Chinese representative Mo Dehui to sell the Chinese Eastern Railway. However, these negotiations were interrupted by the Manchurian Incident. For these reasons, we proposed to sell the railway. Our proposal is a demonstration of Soviet Russia's emphasis on peace, and the Peiping-Shenyang Agreement does not give China the right to redeem the railway before a certain period, nor does it restrict Soviet Russia from selling the railway to any country, especially to a country that is now in Manchuria and fulfilling the responsibilities China assumed under the Peiping-Shenyang Agreement. China has been unable to fulfill its responsibilities in Manchuria for eighteen months, so it has lost the moral right to protest the sale of the Chinese Eastern Railway. Litvinov also said that the Chinese Ambassador to Moscow, Dr. Yan Huiqing, has tacitly acknowledged that China no longer has the ability to fulfill its obligations in Manchuria. (Reuters, 12th)

(Moscow) The Soviet Union did indeed propose selling the Chinese Eastern Railway to Japan or "Manchukuo." This was confirmed by Soviet Foreign Minister Litvinov in his answers to questions from TASS. Litvinov said, "In my conversation with Japanese Ambassador Ota, I did mention the serious situation of the Chinese Eastern Railway caused by the actions of the 'Manchukuo' authorities, and the issue of its potential to increase the disputes between the Soviet Union and Japan-'Manchukuo'. In order to find a possible solution to the dispute, I mentioned the possibility of 'Manchukuo' redeeming the Chinese Eastern Railway, meaning that the Soviet Union would sell the Chinese Eastern Railway to the Manchukuo authorities as the most urgent method to resolve the current difficulties. The Chinese government did send a telegram inquiring about this matter, opposing the Soviet government selling the Chinese Eastern Railway to anyone other than the Chinese government. The Chinese ambassador also sent a memorandum to our country regarding this matter. However, the reasons given by the Chinese government do not conform to the formal treaty commitments and the actual situation. The Sino-Russian and Feng-Russian Agreements do not stipulate China's right to redeem the Chinese Eastern Railway before a certain period, nor do they restrict the Soviet Union from selling the railway to others, especially if the other party is an existing force in Manchuria, and is actually exercising the rights and obligations of the Chinese side in the Sino-Russian and Feng-Russian Agreements. Moreover, in the past eighteen months, the Chinese government and its subordinate forces have, in fact, ceased to be actual co-operators with the Soviet Union on the Chinese Eastern Railway. This possible loss is not due to the Soviet Union. The Chinese government has been unable to exercise its rights and obligations in accordance with the Sino-Russian and Feng-Russian Agreements. In the past eighteen months, the Chinese government has also been unable to keep its representatives on the Chinese Eastern Railway Board of Directors in accordance with the treaty. The Chinese government has been unable to report the Manchurian authorities' violations of the Chinese Eastern Railway's interests, nor has it attempted to protect the normal operation of the railway. Therefore, the Chinese government's failure to fulfill its obligations under the Sino-Russian and Feng-Russian Agreements in the past eighteen months has caused it to lose the formal and moral rights obtained from the agreement. When the current Chinese Ambassador to Moscow, Dr. Yan Huiqing, and I negotiated the resumption of Sino-Soviet diplomatic relations in Geneva, Ambassador Yan proposed that both sides exchange documents acknowledging the inviolability of the Sino-Russian and Feng-Russian Agreements. I accepted this proposal, but with a reservation, saying that the situation in Manchuria was changing and that the Chinese government should not lose the possibility of fulfilling its treaty responsibilities. At that time, the Chinese government opposed this reservation, because it was impossible in reality. I believe that the above proves that the Chinese government cannot oppose the Soviet Union's sale of the Chinese Eastern Railway, especially selling it to the Manchurian authorities. As for the Soviet Union's motives for selling the Chinese Eastern Railway, a few can be mentioned as follows: The Tsarist government's construction of the Chinese Eastern Railway in foreign Manchurian territory was undoubtedly for imperialist purposes. The Soviet government never had such purposes. After the October Revolution, the Chinese Eastern Railway ceased to be a tool of aggression. However, because the construction cost of the railway came from the Soviet people, the Soviet government had to protect its ownership and interests on the railway. The Soviet government always wanted to sell the railway to China, but the latter was unable to purchase it. Therefore, in order to protect its ownership and interests on the railway, the Soviet government changed the railway into a purely commercial operation, and because it passed through foreign territory, it gave the owner of that territory equal management rights and half of the profits to show fairness. However, the Chinese Eastern Railway often became a source of disputes between the Soviet Union, China, and Manchuria. We can all recall the conflict on the Chinese Eastern Railway in 1929. To remove this source of conflict, the Soviet government negotiated with the representatives of Shenyang and the Chinese government, Mo Dehui, in 1930 to sell the Chinese Eastern Railway. These negotiations were interrupted in the autumn of 1931 due to the Manchurian Incident. Now the issue of selling the Chinese Eastern Railway has matured again. For the reasons mentioned above, the Soviet Union proposed to sell the Chinese Eastern Railway. Our proposal has repeatedly shown the peaceful intentions of the Soviet government. We believe that those who oppose this are doing so out of a desire to see the relationship between Japan and Russia or Russia and Manchuria become strained," (TASS, 11th).

Rudy Reports to the Council

Eastern Section Plunged into Terror

(Moscow) News received here from Blagoveshchensk says that Rudy, the director of the Chinese Eastern Railway, made a report to the Chinese Eastern Railway Council on May 7, describing the disturbances suffered by the eastern section of the Chinese Eastern Railway in recent months, which are extremely terrifying, and that work is almost impossible to carry on. At the same time, he praised the railway employees for continuing to maintain operations under constant threat, and finally requested the Council to take appropriate measures to protect the safety of the railway and ensure the normal operation of the entire line. According to Rudy's report, from the beginning of 1932 to May 5, 1933, the Chinese Eastern Railway suffered enormous losses, with 56 people killed, 825 injured, and 593 kidnapped. Most of the kidnapped employees who were released were unable to work due to severe abuse, and most are still under medical treatment. Those who have not been released are still enduring abuse. During the same period, more than 1,000 railway workers were robbed, 50 locomotives, 958 passenger cars, and 855 freight cars were destroyed, and the railway track was damaged in 53 places, covering about 4,000 meters. In addition, 124 civilian houses were destroyed, and postal and telegraph offices were attacked 775 times. The total amount of this destruction and the losses suffered by the railway due to the suspension of passenger and freight transport amounted to several million rubles. In the more serious incidents of destruction, locomotives and passenger and freight cars collapsed on the side of the road and have not yet been repaired. In fact, most of the bridges and tunnels that should have been guarded were not guarded, and as a result, they were taken advantage of and destroyed. Furthermore, most of the stations on the Eastern Line had no guards, or if they did, they did not perform their duties. At stations such as Samokhvalovo and Hengdaohezi, the collected funds were often stolen, and thieves dared to swagger openly in the stations, treating the railway police as if they did not exist, and were able to use the railway's post office telegrams without hindrance. Rudy went on to describe the admirable way in which the railway workers risked their lives and endured hunger to carry out their work, and then listed the measures he had proposed to prevent railway incidents, namely: (1) Passenger and freight cars should only be allowed to run during the daytime; (2) The speed of trains between Imanpo and Muling should be slowed down; (3) A reconnaissance car should be used in front of passenger cars; (4) The security of passenger cars should be strengthened, etc. However, he said that these measures had no effect at all, and the banditry suffered by the Eastern Railway continued to increase. Rudy recently proposed the following matters for the Council's adoption: (1) Reduce the number of passenger cars between Imanpo and Suifenhe to two per week; (2) Reduce freight cars to an extreme extent, to the point of abolishing passenger car regulations; (3) Close all unguarded stations; (4) Instruct the railway police headquarters to add armored vehicles to all passenger car runs; (5) Add guards to freight cars; (6) Add armed guards in certain sections. Rudy said that the above items are also not the final solution, as they would be costly and may not be sufficient to guarantee normal traffic. Therefore, the Council should take the necessary measures to establish an appropriate security county to fully guarantee the safe operation of the entire eastern section of the Chinese Eastern Railway. (TASS, 12th)

Deadline for Russia to Return Locomotives Expires

Japan's Reply to Russia is Being Drafted

Instigating the Puppet to Come Forward for Negotiations

(Tokyo) The Japanese authorities continue to say that Japan wants to place Russian-"Manchu"-Japanese relations on a peaceful foundation. Foreign Ministry Spokesman Discusses

The Russian Sale of the Chinese Eastern Railway

Regardless of Treaties and International Faith

Will Lodge a Serious Protest in the Coming Days

(Nanjing) A spokesman for the Foreign Ministry discussed the Chinese Eastern Railway affair. When Ambassador Yan met with Soviet Deputy Foreign Commissar Karakhan on the 9th to deliver a note, Karakhan denied that the Soviet government had proposed to sell the railway. However, on the 11th, Soviet Foreign Commissar Litvinov openly declared when meeting with reporters that China had lost its rights under the 1924 Sino-Soviet Agreement, and bluntly admitted that it was preparing to sell the Chinese Eastern Railway. It is truly astonishing that he should reverse himself so quickly in just two days. Our government will lodge a serious protest in the coming days, refuting this with reason in order to protect our country's rights. It is deeply regrettable that this event, which disregards treaties and international faith, has occurred only a few months after the resumption of Sino-Soviet diplomatic relations. (Central News Agency, 12th)

(Nanjing) After our Foreign Ministry instructed Ambassador Yan to send a note regarding Soviet Russia's sale of the Chinese Eastern Railway's rights and interests to Japan, Soviet Foreign Commissar Karakhan replied to Ambassador Yan, saying that the Soviet Union did not propose to sell the Chinese Eastern Railway. However, news came that Soviet Foreign Commissar Litvinov yesterday issued a declaration saying that Soviet Russia was preparing to sell the Chinese Eastern Railway, and that the Sino-Soviet Agreement had become invalid in fact because the Chinese government had not sent directors to the railway for eighteen months, and that the Chinese government had no right to exercise its functions on the railway. Therefore, the sale of the railway by Soviet Russia was legally and morally flawless. Our diplomatic community is extremely indignant about this. Litvinov's declaration and Karakhan's reply were only one day apart, but they were completely contradictory, showing that Soviet Russia's diplomacy is completely untrustworthy. Moreover, Soviet Russia wants to sell the railway, but is shifting the responsibility to our country. Its viciousness is evident. It is truly unfortunate that this action by the Soviet government has occurred at the beginning of the resumption of relations between China and Russia. It is difficult to predict what kind of impact this will have on the diplomacy of the two countries. It is reported that our government will lodge a strong protest on this matter. Furthermore, according to diplomatic circles, although Soviet Russia has clearly indicated that it wants to sell the Eastern Railway, there is still no concrete agreement between Japan, Russia, and the puppet regime on this matter. Although Soviet Russia wants to avoid conflict with Japan as much as possible, and the cunning Japanese are hesitant and satisfied with gaining the railway, it is feared that they will not be able to buy it so smoothly. Therefore, Japan will still remain behind the scenes, and the puppet organization in the Northeast will come forward to cause trouble with Russia in order to achieve its goal of forcibly occupying it. (Central News Agency, 12th)

Attending the Washington Conference

Japanese Representative Ishii Passes Through Honolulu

Singing the Praises of the East Asian Monroe Doctrine

Saying Japan is at War for Peaceful Development

If the United States Recklessly Interferes, They Will Not Hesitate to Go to War

Honolulu: Japanese representative Viscount Ishii, who will attend the Washington Conference, passed through here today, delicately suggesting to local people that the United States should not interfere in Japan's Asian plans, and saying that Japan's military actions in Manchuria are part of a peaceful development plan, which immediately caused surprise and discussion among the people of the island. When reporters met with Ishii, they first asked him to explain what he called the Far East Monroe Doctrine. Ishii replied that Japan's general policy in the Far East could not be explained in a short time, and that the words about the Monroe Doctrine were also misinterpretations. He then spoke at length about Japan's determination to develop peacefully in Asia, saying that his previous explanation of the issue had been clearly misunderstood, leading to the talk of the Monroe Doctrine. He also said, "I dare say that there is very little possibility of war between the United States and Japan. Only two things are enough to create a situation that would lead to war: one is if Japan foolishly interferes in the affairs of the Western Hemisphere, and the other is if the United States interferes in Japan's peaceful development in Asia." A reporter immediately questioned whether Japan's actions in Manchuria were also part of the development process. Ishii replied that Japan's necessary actions in Manchuria were also part of the development process. At this time, military actions and other events undertaken by Japan are phenomena that occur simultaneously with the establishment of a new state, in order to protect the rights of the new state and Japan's interests. He further guaranteed that Japan has no intention of aggression or belligerence, but only wants to obtain the right to peaceful development without interference. However, Ishii did not specify a definite area where the so-called peaceful development of the Japanese will end, wanting the Americans to speculate for themselves. Finally, Ishii also said that Japan has many problems that are quite different from those encountered by Western countries, but at the moment, all parties must make some concessions in order to restore economic stability, although he believes that the economic conference will be successful. (National News Agency, 11th)

US Navy

Implements Austerity Policy

(Washington) U.S. Navy Secretary Swanson continued to cut Navy expenses today, saying that all naval garrisons along the coast must strictly practice austerity. The plan he proposed includes merging 14 radio stations, closing three shipyards on the Atlantic coast, and reducing funding for naval hospitals and prisons, in order to save on unnecessary expenses. However, there will be no changes to naval garrisons in the Pacific, communication agencies between San Francisco, Pearl Harbor, and Cavite, and radio stations on the South Pacific island of Samoa. Only a few radio stations on the Pacific and Atlantic coasts of the United States will be merged. (National Electric, 11th)

Disarmament Turns Danger into Safety

Five Powers Accept Compromise Plan

General Committee Meets on Monday

Whether it Will Pass is Still in Doubt

Reuters, Geneva, 12th - Henderson's compromise plan to save the disarmament conference from deadlock has been accepted by representatives of the five major powers. If it is approved by the General Committee on Monday, the deadlock can be eased. However, British and German opinions are still not close, but the scope of Germany's demands can be revealed to the world.

Reuters, Geneva, 12th - Henderson, Chairman of the Disarmament Conference, made efforts today to reconcile British and German opinions. It is reported that a compromise plan has been devised, and the General Committee will be convened on the 15th of this month to discuss both troop strength and material disarmament issues. It is reported that this plan can be accepted by the German representative Nadolny. It will be submitted to the core group tomorrow. Whether it can gain majority approval is still in doubt.

Five-Power Meeting Fails Again

Reuters, Geneva, 12th - The second meeting of the five powers to discuss the disarmament conference deadlock failed again last night. There is still no understanding on the procedures to be adopted. Representatives of the five powers will report to the core committee today. The General Committee of the Disarmament Conference will probably consider the situation when it meets on Saturday and Sunday.

Reuters, Geneva, 11th - The Disarmament Conference is now certainly on the verge of crisis. Although the British representative Eden and the German representative Nadolny have held private talks repeatedly since the disarmament conference reached a deadlock three days ago, they have ultimately failed to reach any understanding. The German Foreign Minister's shocking statement that if the disarmament conference fails, Germany will rearm has further widened the rift in Geneva. The five powers met this afternoon, chaired by Henderson. The British representative Eden reported on the failure of the negotiations. The five powers will meet again tonight to continue discussions, but it is generally expected that a final plan will not be found.

Havas, Geneva, 11th - In recent days, the British representative has repeatedly held talks with the German representative Nadolny on the issue of European military system unification. Today, representatives from the United States, Italy, and France held a meeting from 5:00 PM to 7:00 PM, chaired by Henderson. He talked with the British representative Eden and the German representative Nadolny one after another. The British representative reported the situation of his contact with Nadolny to the representatives of the three countries, saying that although several consultations had been held, no results had been achieved, and he was very sorry. Nadolny told the representatives that although he seemed to accept the European military system unification plan in pure theory, the various reservations and unacceptable conditions put forward by the United Kingdom were in fact equivalent to a rejection. Therefore, what is currently being discussed is what path should be taken after the disarmament conference. Representatives of the major countries believe that since the situation is already like this, the situation should be submitted to the Presidium and the General Committee successively for clear discussion in order to accurately prove the differences of opinion and determine the responsibilities to be borne by the German government. The representatives of Britain and France are especially advocating this. The representatives will reconvene at 9:00 PM to conclude the talks. It is estimated that the representatives will advocate convening the Presidium of the Disarmament Conference tomorrow afternoon and the General Committee on Saturday to determine the fate of the Disarmament Conference.

German Foreign Minister's Strong Tone

Reuters, Berlin, 11th - The German Leipzig Newspaper published an article today by German Foreign Minister Neurath, predicting the failure of the disarmament conference. At that time, the German government will rearm. The article stated that discussions in Geneva have been going on for fifteen months, but the result has shown that Germany's demand for military equality has not been achieved. The reason is that countries with substantial armaments have no sincerity in disarmament. The general arms limitation or reduction within the scope of the British plan, no matter what its form, and even if such a reduction is made, it still forces Germany to supplement its armaments. Although the British plan is welcome as a practical effort towards a practical solution, it is not satisfactory to Germany in terms of the details of implementing or recognizing Germany's demand for equality. Therefore, the British plan still needs to be modified on these two points.

British Secretary of State for War Sharply Criticizes

Reuters, London, 11th - Secretary of State for War Hailsham said in the House of Lords today regarding the disarmament issue that if Germany is unwilling to participate in the discussion of the British proposal or withdraw from the disarmament conference, then Germany is directly rejecting the implementation of the promised proposals and will bear the responsibility for the failure of disarmament. He hopes that Germany will adopt a more reasonable attitude. Even if Germany does not want to change its attitude, it may not necessarily withdraw from the disarmament conference. However, if Germany actually withdraws from the disarmament conference, what path will other countries take? This is truly an event worthy of the most serious consideration. In his personal opinion, the legal result will be that Germany must be bound by the provisions of the Treaty of Versailles. Any act of rearmament is an act of undermining the treaty and will bring the punitive clauses contained in the treaty into effect. If Germany withdraws from the disarmament conference and declares that it does not want to be bound by the Treaty of Versailles, then he believes that Germany's neighbors may not recognize Germany's behavior as satisfactory and be able to agree to a greatly reduced disarmament method.

French Foreign Ministry Maintains Calm

Reuters, Paris, 11th - Tonight's newspapers published in large characters the German Foreign Minister Neurath's statement that if the disarmament conference fails, Germany will rearm, but the French Foreign Ministry remains calm, saying that the German Foreign Minister's paper is only another demonstration by Germany.

Havas, Lyon, 11th - Former Prime Minister Herriot declared that he would explain the outline of the foreign policy of the Radical Socialist Party (i.e., the current government party) at an appropriate time. He also said that British Prime Minister MacDonald recently declared in the House of Commons, "The US government is prepared to assist Europe in maintaining security. If the disarmament conference can achieve concrete results, the United States can participate in a consultation treaty, so that countries feeling the danger of war can increase security."

He expressed great pleasure at MacDonald's statement that the United States can participate in international actions to maintain security, which is extremely important. From MacDonald's words, it can be seen that Britain has already understood this.

Havas, Geneva, 12th - Czech Foreign Minister Benes arrived here this morning.

Havas, Romanian Capital, 12th - Romanian Foreign Minister Titulescu departed last night to Geneva to participate in the work of the Disarmament Conference and to prepare for the convening of the Standing Political Conference of the Little Entente countries.

Commissioner's Office for Western Frontier Propaganda

Organizational Regulations Passed

Yesterday's Legislative Yuan Meeting

(Nanjing) The Legislative Yuan held its 17th meeting of the third session on the 12th, attended by more than 60 people including Wang Qi, Tang Youren, and Gongjue Zhongni. Sun Ke chaired the meeting, with Liang Hancao as the secretary-general. The organizational regulations of the Commissioner's Office for Western Frontier Propaganda were discussed and passed. (Twelfth Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The original text of the organizational regulations of the Commissioner's Office for Western Frontier Propaganda, passed by the Legislative Yuan at its 17th meeting on the 12th, is as follows: (Article 1) The Commissioner's Office for Western Frontier Propaganda is directly under the Executive Yuan and is responsible for propaganda affairs in the Western Frontier. (Article 2) The Commissioner's Office for Western Frontier Propaganda shall have the following two divisions: (1) General Affairs Division; (2) Propaganda Division. (Article 3) The General Affairs Division may establish sections to handle the following matters: (1) Receiving, dispatching, distributing, drafting, and safekeeping of documents; (2) Revenue and expenditure of funds and preparation of budgets and final accounts; (3) Purchase, safekeeping, and distribution of public supplies; (4) Other matters not under the jurisdiction of the Propaganda Division. (Article 4) The Propaganda Division may establish sections to handle propaganda affairs. (Article 5) The Commissioner for Western Frontier Propaganda, specially appointed, shall manage the affairs of the office and supervise the staff. (Article 6) The Commissioner's Office for Western Frontier Propaganda shall have four secretaries, two specially appointed and two recommended, who shall handle confidential matters under the order of the Commissioner. (Article 7) The Commissioner's Office for Western Frontier Propaganda shall have two division chiefs specially appointed, four to six section chiefs recommended, and eight to twelve staff members appointed. (Article 8) The Commissioner's Office for Western Frontier Propaganda may employ staff as appropriate. (Article 9) The Commissioner's Office for Western Frontier Propaganda may hire honorary advisors and honorary consultants. (Article 10) The detailed rules for the operation of the Commissioner's Office for Western Frontier Propaganda shall be drafted by the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission and submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval. (Article 11) These regulations shall be implemented from the date of promulgation. (Twelfth Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Nanjing) At the 17th meeting of the Legislative Yuan on the morning of the 12th, Committee member Peng Yangguang proposed that Executive Yuan President Wang should be invited to the Yuan to report in order to clarify how the administrative authorities should respond to the urgent national crisis. A similar bomb was also found in the US Consulate here on Tuesday evening. The police are now investigating. According to the Japanese, this was done by the Chinese in the hope of inciting the United Kingdom and the United States to oppose "Manchukuo." (Twelfth Reuters Dispatch)

League of Nations Committee Telephonically Inquires

Reasons for Paraguay's Declaration of War

National News, Geneva, 11th - The Three-Nation Committee appointed by the Council of the League of Nations to consider the dispute between Paraguay and Bolivia decided today to telegraph the Paraguayan government to inquire about the reasons for the formal declaration of war. The Committee also decided at the same time that the President of the Council of the League of Nations should convene a meeting of the Council as soon as possible, and an extraordinary meeting of the Council could be convened at the beginning of next week.

National News, Paraguay Capital, 11th - After Paraguay and Bolivia formally declared war, the Paraguayan government issued its first war report today, claiming that a Bolivian regiment began to attack, and after a fierce attack by the Paraguayan army, the entire regiment was annihilated.

Franco-Canadian Trade Agreement Signed

Havas, Ottawa, Canada, 11th - At noon today, the French Minister and the Canadian government signed a commercial agreement, Canada giving France most-favored-nation treatment and reducing import tariffs on many goods, France giving Canadian goods the lowest tariff rate.

German to Implement Equal Land Rights

Reuters, Berlin, 12th. The National Socialist Party today proposed a bill, intending to start with the state of Prussia, to distribute land to farmers, and then gradually promote it throughout the country. According to the initiators of this bill, since German farmers were freed from the bonds of the Napoleonic Wars, this is the most important change in German law. The bill stipulates that farmland will be divided into several squares, each limited to the amount of land that a farming family can cultivate, and free sale is prohibited. Those who own this land are only allowed one son to inherit it. This farmer must be of Germanic blood, neither Jewish nor of a colored race. If this farmer marries a non-Germanic person, their descendants will lose the right to inherit the property.

Japanese Troops Advance Again, Occupying Luan Dong, Threatening Beiping and Tianjin (Reached)

Plotting to Cross the River and Invade Westward After Occupying Changli and Qian’an

Bombing Miyun, Ji County, and Yutian, Disturbing Our Rear

Wan Fulin, He Zhuguo, and Others All Arrive in Beiping to Confer

Special dispatch from Beiping: The Japanese army's ambitions are unpredictable. On one hand, they are sending personnel to collude with traitors in Tianjin, plotting disturbances. On the other hand, they are mobilizing large armies for a large-scale invasion. The eastern route is invading Luan Dong again, and the northern route is attacking south from the important passes of the Great Wall at Xifengkou and Gubeikou, threatening Beiping and Tianjin. The western route is mobilizing troops to invade Chahar, attacking our defenses, attempting to complete the conspiracy of making North China a state in the shortest possible time. At the very least, they intend to break through our important military bases in North China before the green crops rise, preventing us from counterattacking. This is because the weather is gradually getting hotter, and vegetation is flourishing. Soon, the green crops will rise. If the Japanese army does not take this opportunity to wreak havoc and actively oppress us to submit to their violence, then it will be particularly difficult militarily later on. In order to quickly realize their conspiracy, the Japanese army has already spent heavily in Tianjin to buy off traitors and organize various group armies as internal and external collaborators. They are also using the excuse of our army entering Luan Dong to launch a large-scale offensive, carrying out a general attack on the evening of the 7th. One route advanced from Jianchangying to Qian'an, one route attacked Funing from Jielingkou, and one route advanced westward along the Pingyu Avenue, flanking our garrison on the Beining Line. At the same time, the Japanese army's Luhe unit on the Beining front led armored car formations to pressure our army. Since the Japanese army withdrew from Lulong, Qian'an, Funing, and Changli in Luan Dong last month, in order to maintain local order, a part of Wang Yizhe's army entered Lulong and Qian'an to maintain law and order. On the Beining Line, only He Zhuguo's cavalry regiment of a thousand men, with armored cars named Henan, Huguang, etc., patrolled the line to maintain transportation. The troops at the front were not very numerous. On the Jielingkou front, the enemy attacked Funing from the Zhangjiamafang area on the 7th, engaging our few troops. In order to ensure the safety of our right flank, our army withdrew to the highlands north and southeast of Lulong on the night of the 7th. On the Qian'an front, the enemy attacked from Jianchangying, and clashes occurred near Qian'an and the Lujialuotun area. At the same time, multiple enemy aircraft flew over Qian'an, dropping bombs back and forth. At dawn on the 8th, the enemy army attacked Qian'an in multiple directions, with artillery and aircraft bombing the city, dropping more than 500 shells. Fires broke out in the city, and the northeast corner of the city was also destroyed. There were many casualties among soldiers and civilians. After fierce fighting until yesterday, our army withdrew westward from Qian'an. On the Lulong front, after Funing, Qian'an, and other places fell, the enemy concentrated its forces to attack Lulong. Yesterday, there were clashes in various places northeast, east, and southeast of the county seat. Our army had few troops in Lulong, and there was no defensible terrain, so they also withdrew west of the Luan River at night, holding the original position west of the Luan River. On the Beining Line, the Japanese army began to pressure us on the 7th, flanking along the Pingyu Avenue and advancing westward along the railway with armored cars. On the 7th, they advanced to Danashi, southwest of Qinhuangdao, and had minor contact with our army. On the 8th, they advanced to Beidaihe Liushouying. Yesterday morning (9th), they attacked our line 20 li east of Changli again. Our armored cars were on alert between Zhangzhuang and Liushouying. North of Changli, the enemy advanced along the Pingyu Avenue, also reaching a point more than 20 li from Changli. The enemy who occupied Lulong last night crossed the Qinglong River this morning (10th) and continued to pressure the troops on the east bank of the Luan River. Changli was surrounded by the enemy last night. Our army left only a few cavalry in Luan Dong, and most of them had crossed the river, still holding the original position west of the Luan River last month for operational convenience, confronting the enemy. In order to intimidate our rear, the Japanese army sent multiple aircraft to Yutian, Fengrun, and Shaheyi yesterday to drop bombs, causing considerable losses to the residents. Starting at dawn this morning, two enemy aircraft bombed Miyun three times, and then another aircraft came and dropped several bombs, causing heavy losses to merchants and civilians. This morning, four aircraft also went to Ji County and dropped six bombs, killing more than ten people. At the same time, aircraft also went to Bijia Mountain, Jiuzhong Mountain, and other places to drop bombs. In recent days, the enemy troops in Gubeikou and Xifengkou have greatly increased, showing signs of further attacks. Yesterday, on the Nantianmen front, an enemy aircraft repeatedly reconnoitered our Xinkailing position, dropping bombs three times. This afternoon, more than a hundred enemy cavalry and a battalion of infantry moved towards Heilongtan. The situation in that area is gradually becoming tense again.

Since the outbreak of the Eastern military emergency, the Japanese side initially warned us, using the excuse of our army entering Luan Dong, seemingly taking the form of negotiations. Later, because our side could not accept their unreasonable demands, the war broke out. He Zhuguo came to Beiping twice to request instructions on how to deal with Luan Dong. This morning, Wan Fulin also rushed back from the front to confer. This afternoon, Wan, He, Fu, Shang, and other senior generals all went to Jurentang to confer with Ke Yingqin on Luan Dong and defense plans for all routes. The content is extremely important. In order to consolidate the front line, our army still abandons Luan Dong and retreats to defend Luan Xi. If the Japanese army crosses the river again and advances westward, our army will fight to the death, regardless of success or failure. The attitude of the generals is unusually firm, and the morale of the troops at the front is also very high.

He Yingqin told foreign reporters last night that the Japanese army, using the excuse of our army entering Luan Dong, launched a large-scale invasion and expanded the scope. All responsibility should be borne by the Japanese side. When the Japanese army withdrew last month, a part of our Wang Yizhe's army entered Lulong, Funing, Qian'an, and other places to maintain order, and only a thousand cavalry from He Zhuguo's unit patrolled the Beining Line to maintain transportation. There were no other actions. The Japanese side is actually using this as an excuse, and their deception is evident. (May 10th)

The Overwhelming Military Pressure on Guyuan (Continued)

Special Correspondent of This Newspaper, Guo An

(3) County Magistrate Cai Complains Endlessly

After coming out of the military headquarters, I went to the county government again and sat in County Magistrate Cai Qingchan's office. In an atmosphere of sorrow, County Magistrate Cai Qingchan sometimes frowned tightly and sometimes forced a wry smile, very sincerely revealing the suffering of the people of Guyuan County from their inability to make a living.

The Fifth Team of the Red Swastika Society Treats Wounded Civilians at the Temporary Treatment Center in Qian'an

"Guyuan was established as a county in the fifth year of the Republic of China. On August 4th of that year, it moved from the original county seat of Dushikou to Guyuan. The construction of the county seat began in the fourteenth year and was completed in the sixteenth year. The shape of Guyuan is narrow and long because of the division by the Great Wall. It is about forty li wide from east to west and four hundred li long from north to south. It borders Duolun to the northeast, Baochang to the northwest, Zhangbei County to the west, Chicheng and Yanqing to the southwest, Huairou and Miyun to the southwest, Luanping to the southeast, and Fengning to the east.

The land tax in Guyuan is very light. The regular tax and surtax average only about six yuan per mu. The total amount of cultivated land in the county is nearly 10,000 qing (one qing is about ten mu), and the treasury has 27,000 yuan. The annual collection of land tax can yield about 80%. The monthly administrative expenses are more than 690 yuan, the judicial expenses are about 300 yuan, and the four bureaus and various schools require a total of 3,500 yuan. In addition, the local police and security forces need 3,000 yuan per month, and temporary expenses also amount to about 1,000 yuan per month. However, since last year, the Maintenance Committee has been established to supply provisions to the troops, and all expenses have been increasing day by day. (The Maintenance Committee is managed locally, with expenses distributed throughout the county according to land area.)

The county has more than 15,000 households, with a population of 100,000 men, women, and children. Most of them migrated from Shanxi, Shandong, and Hebei provinces, and there are very few natives. Mongol banner people account for only one or two percent. About 90% of the people are engaged in agriculture, and very few are engaged in industry and commerce. As for literacy, it goes without saying. Speaking of education in this county, there are only three complete primary schools and one normal training institute. The backwardness of culture can be imagined.

There are no large businesses on the county street. There are only a dozen or so small stalls and shops in the city. The main agricultural product in the first and second districts is naked oats, with some wheat, and other crops such as sesame seeds, rapeseed, buckwheat, and peas. There are also sheepskin, wool, fox fur, and medicinal materials such as red peony root, Scutellaria baicalensis, Saposhnikovia divaricata, Plantago asiatica, Astragalus propinquus, Strychnos nux-vomica, Anemarrhena asphodeloides, Atractylodes lancea, and Glycyrrhiza uralensis. The third and fourth districts have relatively more agricultural products, including wheat, sorghum, soybeans, millet, rice, silkworm silk, honey, and almonds, but they are all underdeveloped. The third and fourth districts are mostly mountainous and suitable for planting trees and fruit trees, but unfortunately, there is no management. This is the general situation of this county. The current situation is even more unbearable. This county has always been famous for its poverty. Since the fifteenth year, it has suffered successive droughts, and bandits are everywhere. In the twentieth and twenty-first years, although the harvests were not bad, the low grain prices hurt the farmers, and the poverty of the locality was not solved at all. Naked oats are the main crop in this county, and the price is the cheapest, selling for only 1.8 yuan per stone, so the quality of the year does not make much of a difference. The income of the people depends entirely on the pastureland, because this county is a natural pastureland. Animal husbandry is a sideline for the people, and every household is like this. Every large household has thousands or tens of thousands of cattle, sheep, donkeys, and horses, and even small households have dozens or hundreds of heads. However, recently, the bandits have been too rampant, and there are no regular troops stationed to suppress them. The local security police cannot provide adequate protection, so the livestock of the people are robbed by the bandits. Therefore, the people dare not engage in animal husbandry anymore. In this way, large households decline, and small households become so poor that they have nothing to eat. Recently, with the increase in taxes and the heavy burden of requisitions, how can the people survive?

You think, the finances of this county are now, needless to say, bankrupt. I have exhausted all methods and means, but it is useless. In the past, after the bandits left, the soldiers came. The people, after escaping, could hardly settle down. The local income relied on the surtax on land tax. Besides that, it was requisitions. The people cannot even afford the regular tax, how can they manage the requisitions? Moreover, with the troops passing through, requisitioning carts, this county was assigned thirty three-horse carts. Because the locality does not have such large carts, it was changed to a requisition from the people to purchase them, with each cart costing 300 yuan, which, together with the delivery fee, would amount to about 10,000 yuan. This county sent twelve carts and was already exhausted. The total number of troops passing through, both before and after, was about 50,000 or 60,000. Some were stationed for two or three days and then left, and some arrived and left immediately. However, the loss from the requisition of vehicles and the provision of supplies for the people

was no less than 20,000 or 30,000. The first and third districts are full of supplies for the troops, but no payment has been given yet. In this way, how can a poor Guyuan County like ours bear it?

The Fifth Team of the Red Swastika Society Provides Relief After the Bombing of Qian'an City by Aircraft

The most important thing is spring plowing. If spring plowing is delayed, the people will all starve to death. But now, wanting to do spring plowing, most of the plowing cattle in every household have been robbed by the bandits. Moreover, with the overwhelming military pressure, there is no seed grain left. How can this difficult problem be solved? Sir, please think of a way for this county. The supply of provisions to the troops in the locality has been going on for three months. The grain stocks are not much left. There are still 20,000 troops from the Tang army and more than 10,000 righteous soldiers stationed in the territory. If this stalemate continues, I am afraid that in less than half a month, both the soldiers and the people will starve." As he said this, he looked like he was about to cry. As I was recording, I asked him if he had any solutions. He frowned again and said, "If there is money, there is a solution. The important problem at the moment is that we must solve the spring plowing, but there are no plowing cattle and no seed grain. What can we do? It would be best if we could approve a relief fund of more than 10,000 yuan, and we could maintain it for the time being."

In this sad mood, I managed to record a complaint-filled account for Guyuan County. But, dear readers, in such a poor situation, can we still resist the enemy and win? Well, friends, wait and see the article "A General Account of the Battle of Chahar." Although you are squatting by that distant and beautiful river, I believe you will have a clear and clear picture of the battle of Chahar. (8th, in Zhangyuan)

A General Account of the Battle of Chahar (Special Correspondent of This Newspaper, Guo An)

(1) A Declaration

The current situation in North China is what ordinary people are concerned about. Of course, under the enemy's fierce artillery fire, who can determine what the outcome will be? Except for those friends who are holding guns, squatting in the trenches day and night, waiting for bombs and shells to arrive, the rest of the people in the rear, who is not opening the newspaper (of course, those who don't read are the exception), shaking their heads, and frowning as they curse? In this chaotic and unclear environment, should we, the comrades and compatriots who are not holding guns, show weakness, or should we "take your gun and rush to the front"? Friends, let's look north for a glance.

The war clouds of Luan Dong are moving sometimes tightly and sometimes slowly, but half of the sky on the northwest corner is being shaken by the enemy's exploding bombs. Aren't we, the compatriots like ants on a hot pot, worried again this week about the sky shaking and about to fall in the northwest corner? Duolun was in a fierce hand-to-hand battle, and finally, due to insufficient reinforcements, it changed to a new position. So, will Guyuan, Zhangbei County, and Zhangjiakou, the transportation line between China and Russia, also suffer the same trampling by the enemy? I am a weak guy squatting behind the gun, holding a pen, so in this half of the big sky on the northwest corner, shouldn't I report as much as possible to the readers about the shaking and firmness of the battle line on the northwest corner, and about small problems related to strategy? Therefore, with a heart full of emotion, I wrote this personal report, but everything in it is the true situation that I heard and saw. So, when readers see this fragmented and unsystematic report, what kind of feeling should they have in their hearts?

(2) The Street Battle of Duolun

Duolun, under the command of Zhao Chengshou's two thousand cavalry, and at the same time under the attack of the Liu Guitang rebel army commanded by the Japanese Kojitsu, and five hundred Japanese cavalry, was abandoned due to insufficient reinforcements. That day (29th), the wind howled furiously, and the enemy's aircraft did not arrive, but the most tragic and cruel street battle took place in the ancient city of Duolun. An old soldier, drunk, said very carelessly,

"We were doing things locally and saw that we couldn't hold on anymore. The defense团 (regiment) in the city gathered rioters and set fires everywhere to attack the guard team of our military headquarters. They probably did this because we had confiscated their weapons, a total of five or six hundred guns, and sent them to our hands. Who knew that these guys would find a lot of guns and fight us. This barrage of artillery, guns, and fire was even more urgent than the front line. Who could resist it? Like a tide, we retreated downwards. On this flat sandy plain, when the cavalry got on their horses, who cared about resisting? At this time, whoever ran fast was the hero. This cavalry force, like a puff of smoke, retreated from different battle lines in Duolun, simply abandoning everything. They ran smoking southwest along the Zhangduo Avenue to Zhangbei County, but near Daliangdi, they gathered for a while, but the dark night made it impossible to gather completely. Fortunately, after the enemy entered Duolun, they did not pursue. The rebel army, who wanted both money and women, reportedly caused the people to cry out when they entered the city. When we arrived in Zhangbei County, it happened that the Jin army originally stationed in Zhangbei had been transferred to the east. The trenches in the north of Zhangbei were very well constructed. If the Liu Guitang rebel army wants to attack again, they will really have to fight him hard. Who cares if he is Chinese or not?" The old soldier said, with saliva flying from his mouth. I couldn't help but have this kind of thought in my heart: "Was the reason for withdrawing from Duolun because they were all Chinese and couldn't bear to kill each other?" (To be continued)

Chen Mingshu Returns to China

Chen Jitang Welcomes Chen Back to Guangdong to Discuss Major Plans Together

Guangzhou Correspondence: Former Chairman of Guangdong Province and Minister of Transportation Chen Mingshu recently returned to China from Europe. On the sixth of this month, he arrived in Hong Kong on the Italian mail ship "Conte Verde". Those from the Guangdong provincial military and political circles who went to Hong Kong to welcome him included Second Army Commander Xiang Hanping, President of the Provincial Bank Shen Zaihe, 19th Route Army Commander Cai Tingkai, and 19th Route Army Generals Tan Qixiu and Zhang Yan, etc. After Chen arrived in Hong Kong, he stayed at Ouyang Ju's residence that evening. Relatives and old friends visited in an endless stream. After Chen met with Xiang Hanping, the representative of the Guangdong authorities, he agreed to come to the province the next day to discuss important political matters with Chen Jitang, the Commander-in-Chief of the First Army Group. Therefore, at 3:00 PM on the 7th, he, along with Xiang Hanping, Cai Tingkai, Tan Qixiu, Ouyang Ju, Shen Zaihe, Yang Jianping, and Mrs. Chen, Zhu Guangzhen, and others, a group of more than ten people, took a special train on the Guangzhou-Kowloon Railway and arrived in the port at 7:30 PM that afternoon. Military and political authorities here and personnel from the rear office of the 19th Route Army all welcomed him at the Dashatou Station. The arrangement of military police and detectives was unusually tight. Chen was wearing an apricot gray wool suit that day, and his spirit was better than when he was in Guangdong before. At the station, he exchanged greetings with the welcomers and then took a car with Cai Tingkai and Xiang Hanping back to his private residence in Dongshan Fangyuan. After a short rest, he went with Cai and Xiang to the Model Village to meet Chen Jitang. The two Chens talked happily when they met. In the evening, Chen Jitang hosted a banquet for Chen in the foreign flower hall of the provincial government, with senior military officers of the First Army Group and members and directors of the provincial government in attendance. During the banquet, Chen Jitang stood up and gave a speech, fully expressing his welcome. Chen also stood up and gave a reply speech. It was not until after 10:00 PM that they dispersed in joy. According to Chen's conversation, this return to Guangdong was at the invitation of Commander-in-Chief Chen Jitang to discuss everything and to see old friends in Guangdong. He will stay for a few days and then decide where to go. Regarding the situation, his proposition is that resisting Japan and saving the country is his long-cherished ambition. The 19th Route Army bears the national mission, and continuing to resist Japan is its duty. Although a part has been transferred to depart, if necessary, all of them can be transferred to the north. In short, the 19th Route Army's spirit of resolutely saving the country will never change, and the will of the entire army is like this. His own proposition is also like this, etc. (May 7th)

The Reason for Wu Peifu's Disbanding of His Guards (Leads)

Sending His Subordinates Back to Their Hometowns Due to Economic Hardship

Special dispatch from Beiping: Wu Peifu is living in seclusion in the old capital, studying Buddhism every day, and his attitude is quite passive. There are still 1,500 of his former guards who did not leave with Wu. Wu's monthly expenses in Beiping require more than 10,000 yuan. When Zhang Xueliang was in Beiping, Zhang personally gave 4,000 yuan per month, but Wu's expenses were huge, and income could not meet expenditure. He had to borrow from here and there, and he could not make ends meet. He felt extremely financially embarrassed. Recently, after being persuaded by friends, and at the same time, in order to save expenses, he decided to send his guards back to their hometowns. The day before yesterday (8th), Wu gathered the officers of his former subordinates in Shijin Garden and told them of his difficulties in sending them away. Most of his subordinates expressed their unwillingness to leave Wu. Later, after the local military and police smoothed things over, Wu's officers and soldiers agreed to hand over their weapons first. On the spot, they handed over seven rifles, 121 carbines, 3,265 rounds of ammunition, 281 hand grenades, 226 broadswords, and many scattered weapons. Fan Naiwu, the commander of the Beiping Gendarmerie, and Ma Qingyu, the captain of the Public Security Bureau's Special Affairs Team, checked and received everything one by one and sent twenty gendarmes and policemen to take care of Wu's residence and the guard headquarters of the Princess Mansion. The confiscated weapons were sent to the Gendarmerie Headquarters for safekeeping yesterday afternoon (9th). After the news of Wu's disbanding of his guards spread, the guards had a slight misunderstanding with Wu's chief of staff, Zhang Fangyan, and a dispute occurred. Zhang was slightly injured as a result. After mediation, the officers and soldiers agreed to be sent away, but they requested Wu to issue a commemorative badge to each person as a souvenir of their return to their fields in the future. Wu also felt that his subordinates had been with the army for many years and had worked hard, so he agreed. Currently, the jewelry store is stepping up the production, preparing to issue them, and it is also decided to issue each officer a severance payment of 30 yuan and each soldier 15 yuan. This expense was borne by friends from all sides, and everyone has already received it. Among his former subordinates, people from the three provinces of Zhili, Shandong, and Henan are the most numerous, and there are also about 300 people from Sichuan and Hunan. After the authorities contacted the railway bureau, they were allowed to ride the train for free, and it was agreed that the repatriation would be implemented today and tomorrow. This morning, the reporter went to Shijin Garden to pay his respects to Wu. He was received by Mr. Xu Tiefeng, who said that Wu's attitude was the same as before. The previous time he came to Beiping at the invitation of Zhang Xueliang was to jointly plan to resist Japan and defend against insults. At present, the central government has an overall plan to resist Japan, and Wu himself can contribute everything in his capacity as a commoner. The guard team was decided to be disbanded due to insufficient funds. From now on, Wu will live in Beiping as a commoner to recuperate and will never go anywhere else. If Wu is needed for anti-Japanese affairs, he will definitely serve the country, going through fire and water. As for the frank attitude of not living in the concession and not relying on foreigners, he will never change his original intention. At the same time, because Wu had been in power for a long time, and his former subordinates were all over the north and south, it is inevitable that some people would borrow his name, and he could not recognize them. It is heard that Wu's current living expenses in Beiping, after Zhang Xueliang left Beiping, are still paid by Chairman Jiang Jun at the rate of 4,000 gold per month to maintain the status quo. (May 10th)

Reasons for the Accusation Against the Magistrate of Rugao County, Songjiang

Qian Zuoyi, a native of the county, was appointed as the magistrate of Rugao County in the past. He assumed office during a time of rampant banditry, which was soon quelled. This time, he was suspended from his duties and transferred to the Zhenjiang Court Prosecutor's Office for investigation. A reporter inquired about the matter, and Magistrate Qian stated that the case was referred to the Civil Service Disciplinary Committee for investigation. He presented the original text of the Civil Service Disciplinary Committee's review, as well as a factual account of the events. According to Qian, after he took office, the 25th Army's Liang Guanying's unit was about to depart for Anhui and directly demanded 80,000 yuan in military pay from the Rugao County government. Magistrate Qian then sought instructions from the provincial government and convened a meeting of gentry and merchants, deciding to borrow from wealthy merchants. He dispatched personnel to expedite the matter at the land registry office. Subsequently, the office reported that Lu Huai's father, Lu Xiaotang, had assets of over 100,000 yuan and suggested borrowing 500 yuan. Lu Huai happened to return to Rugao from school in Shanghai and suddenly went back on his word, only paying 150 yuan. Despite repeated urging, he refused to pay the remaining amount. A report was submitted to the county government, and the head of the first section, Zhou Rongdai, was dispatched to diligently persuade him, but he still refused to pay. An order was issued for him to provide a guarantor and a deadline for payment, but he was not detained. Lu Huai appealed to the Provincial Department of Civil Affairs, which ruled that he should pay 300 yuan. Lu remained dissatisfied and is now appealing to the provincial government, which has not yet been resolved. In the Civil Service Disciplinary Committee's review document, the point of Lu Huai's father providing a guarantor and a deadline for payment was considered evidence of detention. It was argued that if there were no detention, there would be no need for a guarantor. The accused was considered to have admitted that the matter was true. Therefore, a letter was sent to the provincial government to suspend him from his duties and to conduct an investigation in court. Qian has now gone to the province to surrender himself for interrogation and requested access to the original files to clarify the truth.

Open-Air Assassination Case in Taicang

In the open-air temple area of the seventh district of the county, a villager named Pu A'quan, who worked as a farmer, was found dead. His father had passed away early, and his mother had remarried. He had a wife, but although she was not chaste, the couple's relationship was relatively harmonious. On the morning of the sixth of this month, Pu's wife went out to buy vegetables, and A'quan was alone at home. When his wife returned, she suddenly saw A'quan lying in a pool of blood, already dead. The murderer had fled without a trace. Upon closer examination of the body, five knife wounds were discovered, all in vital areas. However, after the incident, the deceased's family and the township head, Pu Jifu, and the local security officer, Pu Shaolin, all concealed the matter from the county government. Now, Wan Baocai, the head of the county's detective team, has heard the news and has dispatched Officer Zhu to secretly investigate and clarify the truth.

Large Gang of Lake Bandits Discovered in Taihu Lake, Suzhou

Recently, lake bandits in the Suzhou area have become rampant, and robbery cases are frequent. The night before last, a bandit boat carrying more than ten bandits was discovered near the Midu Bridge outside the Fengmen Gate of Suzhou. After being pursued by the police, they escaped towards Huangtiandang. That same evening (the 11th) at 8:00 PM, the Xingji Cloth Store in the bustling market of Mudu Town was robbed, with losses exceeding 600 yuan. The bandits fled towards Lion Mountain. News has now arrived that yesterday (the 12th) at 11:00 AM, over twenty lake bandits were discovered in East Taihu Lake, and eighty lake bandits were also discovered in West Taihu Lake, all fully armed, with the intention of carrying out robberies. After receiving the report, the Third District of the Water Police immediately dispatched ten naval ships to pursue and suppress them. The police teams of Wujiang and Wuxian counties also dispatched teams to set out. At the same time, the county government ordered the land and water police teams stationed in the East and West Dongting Mountains to mobilize and encircle the bandits.

Wuxi Land and Water Military Police Protect Cocoon Market

The Jiangsu Provincial Government, in view of the imminent arrival of the spring cocoon season, should prepare in advance for the protection of cocoon merchants and the collection of cocoons. A zoned protection plan has been drafted: (1) Songjiang, Shanghai, Fengxian, and Jinshan counties will be jointly responsible by the First District of the Water Police in coordination with the garrisoned army; (2) Wuxi, Wujin, Yixing, and part of Jiangyin counties, as well as the tombs inside the East, West, and South Mountains of Taihu Lake, will be jointly responsible by the Second District of the Water Police in coordination with the garrisoned army and patrol ships; (3) Changshu, Kunshan, Wuxian counties, and all areas along the Jiangsu-Zhejiang border will be jointly responsible by the Third District of the Water Police in coordination with the garrisoned army; (4) Nantong, Haimen, and the coastal areas of Changshu will be jointly responsible by the Fourth District of the Water Police in coordination with the army; (5) Zhenjiang, Danyang, Jiangning, Yangzhou, and part of Jiangyin will be jointly responsible by the Fifth District of the Water Police and the army; (6) The Provincial Public Security Team on Water, guerrillas, and patrol ships will patrol in their respective areas to supplement the police force; (7) The Department of Civil Affairs will assign the head of the Second District of the Water Police to organize an office in Wuxi, where sericulture is flourishing, to supervise and direct operations. In addition, protection measures will be formulated in accordance with precedents and then ordered to the Wuxi County Government and the Second District of the Water Police for compliance.

Thorough Investigation of the Embezzlement of Stolen Goods by the Local Defense Corps

The Local Defense Corps of the fifth district of the county seized two bandit boats near the Sanhao Bridge on the Xi-Cheng Road in the middle of last month, containing thirty-eight large pigs and sixty silver dollars. Afterwards, Yang Zuxun, the township head and head of the Local Defense Corps, slaughtered one pig to reward the troops and hid twenty-five others, only handing over twelve. The sixty silver dollars were also divided and spent by several members of the corps. The twenty-five large pigs that were embezzled were sold at a low price to the Tan Yaobing and Zou Ahe butcher shops for 30 yuan each, totaling over 700 yuan. Before long, the owner, Tang Rulin, learned of this, investigated the truth in the township, and requested the county government to investigate thoroughly. Yesterday, Magistrate Yan ordered the township head Yang Zuxun and the butcher shop owners Tan Yaobing and Zou Ahe to be brought to court for interrogation. After confirming the facts, they were detained pending punishment.

Changzhou Court Searches Drug Trafficking Organization

Yang Kongyi, the chief prosecutor of the Wujin County Court Prosecutor's Office, and others, led bailiffs and members of the merchant corps patrol team to search a drug trafficking organization at 55 Qingguo Lane at noon on the 11th. As a result, they found a signboard of the Xingji Company, account books, and other items. After the search, the county party headquarters immediately sent a letter to the county court, requesting that the house of the drug trafficking organization be sealed immediately, those responsible be arrested, and a telegram be sent to the provincial party headquarters for approval. A letter was also sent to the First District Public Office to find out the name of the owner of the house of the organization for verification.

Jiangyin Security Commissioner Visits Cheng to Assess Performance

Qiu Mingjiu, a performance assessment commissioner sent by the Provincial Security Committee, arrived in Cheng from Xi the day before yesterday (the 10th). Together with Magistrate Ruan, they discussed and decided to conduct regular examinations of the county's Local Defense Corps by district. Starting on the 11th, they, along with Magistrate Ruan and Police Captain Yin, set out to examine the corps members in each district.

Manager of Tailai Company in Yangzhou Detained

The Tailai Flour Company set up a station in Yangzhou to collect wheat. Because it failed to pay business tax, the Jiangdu Business Tax Bureau sent a letter to the county government, requesting that the manager of the station, Sheng Shanqing, be summoned to the county and be required to pay 920 yuan in business tax according to the business tax regulations. Sheng argued that the wheat flour had already been subject to a special tax, and wheat had long been exempted from taxes. Now, if a business tax is levied for setting up a station to collect wheat, it would be akin to double taxation. In addition to submitting a petition to the Ministry of Finance, he specially petitioned the county government for bail. After receiving the petition, Acting Magistrate Ma stated that the collection of this business tax was based on the request of the Business Tax Bureau. Since a petition had been submitted to the Ministry of Finance, the matter should be handled according to the Ministry's order. It was now instructed that until the Ministry's order was received, a guarantor and a pledge should be obtained and kept in the county for verification.

Nantung Dasheng Factory Labor Strike Resolved

The labor strike at the Tangzha Dasheng Yarn Factory, which had lasted for ten days, has now been resolved through mediation by party and government representatives. The factory resumed operations on the 12th. The county government issued a special notice stating: "The labor strike at the Dasheng Yarn Factory has been suppressed by order of this government, and officials have been sent to investigate. This time, the workers were exploited and went on strike without reason, disrupting local order and cutting off the livelihoods of fellow workers. This government, mindful of the difficulties of the times, will refrain from further investigation for the time being. The factory has now been persuaded to register and verify workers as soon as possible, and it has been ordered to resume operations on the 12th of this month. All male and female workers of the factory must work with peace of mind. If there are any evildoers who persist in their wickedness, obstruct and cause trouble, they will be severely arrested and dealt with according to the law."

Yellow Spear Society in Hefei Opens Fire in Resistance to Opium Suppression

The Yellow Spear Society in the northeastern third, fourth, and fifth district, due to Magistrate Wang leading a team into the countryside to forcibly suppress opium cultivation, gathered over a thousand people, announced their resistance. Magistrate Wang was unable to carry out the suppression at the Longhua Temple in Youfangji. Subsequently, the commander of the 55th Division, Ruan Zhaochang, dispatched the Zhao regiment and Liu battalion to suppress them. The Yellow Spear Society dared to attack the troops, wounding more than ten people. Fire was then opened, resulting in the deaths of dozens of members of the Yellow Spear Society, and the remaining members scattered. Magistrate Wang and Regiment Commander Zhao ordered that no further attacks be made, and they simultaneously advised the public and supervised the suppression of opium seedlings. However, there are rumors that the Spear Society in each district is still reorganizing to resist.
