Sun Dianying's Representative Hosted News Media Yesterday

Reported on the Course of Sun's Army's Resistance Against Japan

Sun Dianying, commander of the 41st Army, recently sent Hu Jiesan, director of the Beiping Office, to Shanghai to report to all circles and receive treatment. Yesterday afternoon, he hosted the news media at Yizhi Xiang, where over fifty reporters from various newspapers attended. During the event, Hu Jiesan reported: "Comrades and brothers, I, Hu Jiesan, have been specially sent by General Sun Dianying to Shanghai to thank all circles for their support and the encouragement of the journalists. I have prepared a simple meal, and I am honored and pleased that you have all come here to discuss matters. During this resistance against Japan, our army was ordered to proceed to Chifeng. Due to the loss of Chengde, our army was suddenly surrounded. Since March 2nd, we have been under increasing pressure from the enemy. We were not only hungry and cold but also had no source of ammunition. After more than twenty days of bloodshed, we finally broke out of the encirclement on March 28th. The casualties among officers and soldiers amounted to several thousand. The details of the battle have been telegraphed to the authorities and disclosed in various newspapers, so you are already aware of them. Over the past month, various groups and comrades, both Chinese and foreign, have provided us with a large number of supplies, money, and ammunition. Our army is deeply grateful for this generosity. Our commander has instructed each department, saying that the only way our army can repay the party and the country is with blood and flesh. Today, I dare to represent all the officers and soldiers of our army with these words to express our gratitude to our compatriots and journalists. However, the work of resisting Japan is very long, and the East is once again tense. Our army has built extremely strong defenses in the area of □□□□, and the soldiers have the determination to die. Our commander has long resolved to coexist with the enemy. If the enemy attacks, we will give them a head-on blow. Even if only one soldier remains, we will fight to the end. However, our army is far away in the northern frontier, and transportation is inevitably slow. Reports on the fighting situation are often incomplete. I hope that the journalists and compatriots from all walks of life will provide our army with guidance and encouragement at any time. The officers and soldiers will work harder to repay you all. This is what our army especially prays for."

The Fourth Batch of Expelled Overseas Chinese from Mexico Returns Home

Fifty-Nine Men, Women, and Children Landed and Went Directly to the Municipal Government to Petition The Overseas Chinese General Association Discovered Funds for Relief Three Representatives Stayed in Shanghai While the Rest Returned to Their Hometowns by Ship

Xinhua News Agency reported that the situation of the anti-Chinese movement in Mexico is extremely serious. All the properties of overseas Chinese in Mexico have been seized and confiscated, and they have been expelled from the country. Three batches have already returned to the country one after another. Yesterday morning, another fourth batch of fifty-nine male and female refugee overseas Chinese returned to the country on the Hoover President of the Da Lai Company. The details are as follows:

Arrival in Shanghai

The Hoover President entered the port at 8:00 AM yesterday morning and docked at the Da Lai Wharf in Bailianjing, Pudong. The Shanghai Overseas Chinese General Association specially sent its general secretary, Peng Can Guang, and more than ten people, including the reception minister Fang Di Fei, to charter a small steamer to Pudong to welcome them and take care of everything. After Peng and others arrived at the Da Lai Wharf, they boarded the Hoover President and first expressed their condolences to the returning refugees, and explained the purpose of initiating the relief effort. All the refugees expressed their gratitude. Subsequently, Peng led the refugees on a small steamer, which arrived at the New Customs Wharf at 9:15 AM and disembarked.

Petition to the Municipal Government

The Overseas Chinese General Association had prepared more than ten cars to transport all the refugees. They drove first to the Municipal Government at Fenglin Bridge to petition. However, due to the large number of people and Mayor Wu's busy schedule, fearing that it would disrupt important official business, refugees elected Zhang Fu Kuan and Huang Zhu Lin as representatives, accompanied by Peng Can Guang, to petition Section Chief Li Da Chao. The rest of the refugees waited in front of the Municipal Government. Li received them, and the refugee representatives first reported on the recent anti-Chinese situation in Mexico and requested that a telegram be sent to the central government to negotiate with the Mexican government as soon as possible. Li expressed that he would relay it to Mayor Wu and submit a request to the central government to issue a serious protest to Mexico. After the petition, the refugees returned in the original dozen or so cars, each with a white cloth flag bearing the words "Global Overseas Chinese General Association Welcomes Expelled Overseas Chinese from Mexico," and circled around Xiafei Road, Jing'an Temple Road, North Sichuan Road, and Zhabei. They returned to the Overseas Chinese General Association on Guizhou Road at 12:00 PM for rest.

Reception Lunch

At 2:30 PM, the Overseas Chinese General Association hosted a lunch at the Xin Xin Restaurant on Nanjing Road to entertain all the refugees, and the chairman of the association, lawyer Wu Cheng Yu, personally hosted the event. Before the meal, all the refugees took a group photo, followed by a meeting. Chairman Wu Cheng Yu announced the reasons for the relief effort, and Huang Zhu Lin was elected from among the refugees to report on the recent anti-Chinese situation in Mexico. He stated that on January 12 of this year, the new governor of Mexico took office and announced an extremely strict anti-Chinese policy, setting a deadline of June 31 of this year for all overseas Chinese (approximately 20,000 people) to leave the country. After the report, Peng Can Guang, the general secretary of the General Association, gave a speech. Peng rose to give a very poignant speech, which moved all the refugees and was greeted with thunderous applause. Speakers such as Fang Di Fei followed.

Formation of a Maintenance Committee

Later, all the refugees unanimously resolved to elect Lin Hui Yao, Lin Wen Li, and Huang Zhu Lin as representatives to stay in Shanghai to request effective relief from the government and all sectors of society, and to form a "Mexican Refugee Maintenance Committee" to unite all returning refugees to work hard to solve the current and permanent suffering. Then, refugee representative Huang Zhu Lin proposed that all the refugees join the Overseas Chinese General Association as members. Everyone applauded and unanimously approved. After the meeting, Chairman Wu Cheng Yu gave a closing speech, and the meeting adjourned at 5:00 PM. All the refugees then returned to the Overseas Chinese General Association for rest.

Issuance of Relief Funds

Subsequently, Wu Zi Yuan, a standing committee member of the association, together with accountant Hong Zhuo Guang, distributed relief funds, allocating ten yuan to each refugee, who signed for receipt. As for the actual situation of the anti-Chinese movement in Mexico, the refugee representatives promised to provide a detailed written report to reporters today.

Original Ship Heads to Hong Kong

Except for the three representatives, the rest of the refugees were accompanied by Fang Di Fei and others on the original ship Hoover President at 9:00 PM last night, which set sail for Hong Kong this morning, returning to their hometowns in Guangdong. According to the refugees, there are still more than two hundred expelled compatriots currently waiting for ships in the United States to return to the country.

List of Refugees

Lei Jin Song, Chen You Geng, Tan Jiu, Du Cai, Ye Ying, Liu Chao, Yang Wang, Huang Hui, Lin Hui Yao, Huang Sheng, Deng Mu, Huang Yu, Li Pan Ye, Wu Si, Wen Jing Tang, Chen Wei, Ma Xi, Chen Yuan Bin, Li Lu Nan, Li Ye, Wu Shi (Mexican wife), Wu Wu Wei, Chen Zhen Zhuo, Li Cai Fu, He Chang Zhi, Zheng Hui, Chen Le, Wu Bai, Lei Xing Zhi, Xie Xiang, Li Jian, Chen Li Yuan, Zhu Shun, Liang Dong Ping, Huang Zhu Lin, Tang Shi Nong, Li Mai, Liu Xiang, Ma Xi's wife (Mexican wife), Zhu Zhi, Liang Da, Li Heng, Lin Wen Li, Wu Bai's wife (Mexican wife), Zhang Rao, Chen Quan, Wu Qu, Li Li, Deng Hua, Zhang Fu Kuan, Chen Ya San, Li Heng, and fifty-nine children, etc.

Yongyuan Licheng Ship Stranded on a Reef in Quanzhou

Telegram States that the First Two Holds have Flooded

Customs Ship Pingqing is Providing Assistance

The Guowen News Agency reported that the Yongyuan Shipping Company at 15 Sijing Road, this port, received a telegram from Keelung stating that the company's Licheng ship was stranded on a reef near Xinghua, Quanzhou, and the first two holds had flooded. A reporter inquired about the details yesterday afternoon.

Yongyuan Manager

The Yongyuan Shipping Company is a joint-stock company, managed by Zhao Song Nian. The head office is in Qingdao, and this port is a branch office. It has four ships: Licheng, Lishun, Yongyuan, and Yuanshun. The Licheng usually travels to the northern and southern seas, such as Dalian, Yingkou, Niuzhuang, Fuzhou, Quanzhou, and Xiamen. A few days ago, it sailed from Niuzhuang to Xiamen. Yesterday morning at 7:00 AM, it suddenly ran aground near Quanzhou Bay, and the impact was very strong, causing the first two holds to flood immediately.

Licheng History

The Licheng was carrying soybean cakes, soybeans, miscellaneous grains, and general cargo from Niuzhuang to Fujian. The ship had a deadweight tonnage of 2,020 tons. The company bought it from a certain Japanese shipping company in this port four years ago for 100,000 yuan. The ship is in good condition, 258 feet long, and was built in 1889. It is currently insured with Lianbao Insurance Company for 80,000 silver dollars. The owner of the ship is Chinese (surname unknown), and there are thirty to forty crew members.

Details of the Stranding

The reason why the Licheng was stranded in Quanzhou Bay is not yet clear. According to the company's speculation, it may have been due to fog in the early morning. According to the first telegram forwarded by the ship from Keelung, the location was at 118.46 degrees east longitude and 24.49 degrees north latitude, near Quanzhou Bay. The first telegram stated that the Licheng ran aground near Quanzhou at 7:00 AM on the 12th and requested that a rescue ship be dispatched immediately. The second telegram, sent at 10:00 AM, was received by the Shanghai Coast Radio Station of the Ministry of Communications and forwarded to the Customs and the company. It stated that the Licheng was stranded, the first two holds had flooded, and the Pingqing ship was rushing to rescue and protect it, with further reports to follow. However, after receiving the first telegram, the company immediately sent a telegram inquiring about the cargo and the cause of the accident, but had not received a reply as of 6:00 PM yesterday.

Attempts to Rescue

Upon hearing the news, Yongyuan immediately contacted Lianbao Insurance to arrange for a rescue ship to go to the rescue in this port, which may depart today. Yesterday afternoon, a reporter visited the company, where they met customs officials. They announced that the Licheng had run aground, and the customs had received two telegrams. The Customs ship Pingqing (Pingching) had already arrived and was doing its best to rescue and protect the ship. They had a telegram that could be sent to the Pingqing ship for inquiries (the two telegrams were the same as those received by the company and were therefore not recorded). The company claimed that the Customs ship Pingqing was providing protection because the area was known to be frequented by pirates.

Raise Funds for National Aviation Salvation

First Day of Boy Scout Mobilization

Yesterday was the first day of the Boy Scout mobilization to raise funds for National Aviation Salvation. At 9:00 AM, the city's Boy Scouts, divided into 51 teams, carrying flags, donation books, and Aviation Association badges and membership cards, went to various roads to solicit donations. When they encountered cars and rickshaws, they stopped them. If the passengers had not yet joined the association, they were immediately persuaded to donate. Receipts and membership cards were issued. Many enthusiastic patriots made generous donations. However, there were also some who were reluctant and evasive. The funds raised by the Boy Scouts were deposited in the Shanghai Bank in each district, and the bank notified the Boy Scout Council. Therefore, the total number of yesterday's results has not yet been tallied. What is known is that the Southeast Boy Scouts raised more than 300 yuan yesterday.

Zhengtai Factory

Donates to Shanghai Workers' Aircraft

The Zhengtai Rubber Factory in this port, which produces Daxipai, Wannianqingpai, Sanbapai brands of galoshes, running shoes, and athletic shoes, is of high quality and low price, and its sales reach across the country. It is one of the leading factories in the country, with over one thousand employees. The factory has a long-standing patriotic enthusiasm. Li Jingcong Discusses the Successful Test Flight of the Guangdong-Hankou Railway

Two More Points Need to be Resolved Formal Opening Expected in Late Summer or Early Autumn

The Eurasia Aviation Company, to open the Guangdong-Hankou air route, had its manager, Li Jingcong, and deputy chief of flight, Walter, leave Shanghai on the 4th for a test flight to Hankou and to inspect the entire route. They returned on the 11th after a successful test flight. Yesterday, Manager Li told a reporter from the Central News Agency that the results of the test flight were very satisfactory. The formal opening of the route is still to be planned in detail. Li's remarks are summarized as follows:

Test Flight Details

Li said that the planning for the Guangdong-Hankou route has been underway for a long time. Merchants in Guangdong urgently need this route, and Minister Zhu of the Ministry of Communications has repeatedly urged its early opening to benefit the people. Therefore, taking advantage of the current lack of development in the Northwest route, a test flight was carried out first. On the morning of the 4th, I and Deputy Chief Walter took the Eurasia No. 5 aircraft to Hankou for a test flight. The aircraft was piloted by Rajai. When passing through Beijing, we stopped for an hour to discuss matters with Minister Zhu and continued to fly on that evening, arriving in Hankou. On the 5th, we flew from Hanam and passed Changsha. Because the airport was small, we did not land and planned to fly directly to Guangzhou. However, when we reached the Jiufeng Mountains, we were forced to turn back to Changsha due to thick fog. On the 6th, we continued to fly south. When passing the Jiufeng Mountains, we flew low through the mountain pass. After exiting the pass, we crossed Shaoguan without stopping and arrived safely in Guangzhou around 3:00 PM. We visited the military and political authorities to humbly request their assistance. After resting for a day, we flew from Guangzhou to Hong Kong on the 8th, planning to extend the route to the port. We specifically visited the British Governor to seek his opinion, and he verbally expressed his welcome. Therefore, we immediately asked the government to assist in the negotiation. On the 9th, we flew north from Hong Kong and arrived in Guangzhou that same day. On the 10th, we arrived in Hankou, and on the 11th, we passed through Beijing and arrived in Shanghai. I stayed in Beijing for half a day to discuss matters with the ministry and took the night train to Shanghai. Chief Walter flew back to Shanghai on the original aircraft on the same day.

Two Difficulties

Li continued to tell the reporter that the test flight was successful, but there were two points that still needed to be resolved: (1) The facilities on the route. At a considerable distance, there must be reserve airfields for takeoff and landing when necessary. Although the Northwest route does not have this equipment, there are many open plains along the way, and it is possible to land anywhere in case of danger. On the other hand, the Guangdong-Hankou route is crisscrossed with fields, all of which are paddy fields. In case of obstacles, it is not possible to land. Many airports must be equipped, but the company cannot afford it on its own. We have been in contact with the Ministry of Communications to request assistance. (2) The mountains in Hunan Province are winding and foggy, and the Jiufeng Mountains are so high that they reach into the clouds, making flying very difficult. We plan to set up radio stations in Yizhang Lushi to report on the weather to indicate where to go and avoid danger.

Summer Navigation

The above two points are now being actively planned. Within one to three months, preparations will be completed, and navigation should be possible by late summer or early autumn. The entire route will serve three stations: Hankou, Changsha, and Guangzhou. Including stopover times, the journey will take approximately six and a half hours. The airports in Changsha and Guangzhou will temporarily use those belonging to the Ministry of Military Affairs, and only land-based aircraft will be used for flights. Shaoguan only has a seaplane base, and it is very small, so a station will not be set up there for the time being. However, this plan is only the southern section of the entire route. There is also a northern section extending north from Hankou, passing through Xiangyang and reaching Xi'an, to connect with the Northwest Line. However, testing and planning of everything must wait until the Canton-Hankou section is officially opened to traffic.

Postal Foundation Case Still Not Fully Resolved

Postal Research Association Continued Meeting Yesterday

Announced Adjournment for One Week

The Postal Economic System Research Committee continued its seventh general meeting yesterday to discuss the outline for consolidating the postal foundation reform. The dispute between the Ministry and the employees regarding the selection and performance evaluation of personnel in the Savings and Remittances Bureau has not yet been resolved. For the sake of prudence, the committee announced an adjournment for one week to seek an appropriate solution. Details are recorded below.

Attendees: The Postal System Research Association held its seventh general meeting at the Municipal Government at 5 pm yesterday. Attendees included committee members Wu Tiecheng, Lin Kanghou, Lin Shi, Pan Gongzhan, Huang Naishu, Tang Shu, Du Yuesheng, and others, totaling seven people. Attending as observers were specialist committee members Wang Wenwei, Li Gan, Lin Zou, Jing Runying, Shen Yangyi, Lou Zuyi, and others, totaling six people. There were also twelve employee representatives from the postal service: Zhu Fan, Kang Yong, Zhang Kechang, Shi Yitang, Qi Jiamou, Zhu Jingsheng, Fan Caicong, Zheng Zhenhuang, Shi Jikuan, Ge Fei, Zhao Shusheng, and Lu Keming, for a total of twenty-five people.

Dispute Unresolved: Regarding the selection and performance evaluation of personnel in the Savings and Remittances Bureau, disputes arose between the Ministry and the employees, which led to delays in resolution. Committee members Lin Kanghou and Pan Gongzhan, along with several employee representatives, went to the Cangzhou Hotel at 10 am yesterday to meet with Minister Zhu to exchange opinions in order to find a solution. The discussion lasted until noon. Subsequently, at 5 pm in the afternoon, the general meeting continued at the Municipal Government. The committee members revised clauses D and E of the second article of the outline for consolidating the postal foundation reform. However, the principle of dual power remained unchanged, and the textual revisions were insufficient to remedy the situation. The Ministry insisted that personnel in the Savings and Remittances Bureau, after being screened, should be treated as additional personnel and not considered postal workers. The employees insisted that personnel in the Savings and Remittances Bureau must pass an examination and be ranked as postal personnel; otherwise, their treatment should not exceed that of postal workers. The discussion continued until about 7:30 pm. The two sides fiercely debated the selection and performance evaluation of personnel in the Savings and Remittances Bureau, and their opinions could not be reconciled. For the sake of prudence, the committee formally announced an adjournment of the meeting for one week to allow both sides to make a final consideration. The meeting is scheduled to continue at the Municipal Government on the 19th, and Lin Kanghou was designated to visit Minister Zhu again to exchange opinions in order to find a solution. If the dispute between the two sides remains unresolved when the meeting continues next week, the committee will submit the opinions of both sides to the Ministry for review.

Soviet Embassy Corrects Report on Remarks

TAS News Agency, local dispatch: Yesterday's local newspaper reported that the content of the conversation between Soviet Ambassador Bogomolov and Chen Gongbo, the Minister of Industry of the Chinese government, in Nanjing on May 10 was not entirely accurate. Regarding China sending a study group to the Soviet Union, it was only mentioned in passing and was not specifically for discussion as reported. Also, regarding China's establishment of a special bureau for trade with the Soviet Union, Mr. Bogomolov stated that the Soviet government considers this approach to be discriminatory towards the Soviet Union.

English and American Labor Unrest Difficult to Resolve, Operations Completely Suspended at Three Factories

Labor Union Requests Convening of General Meeting to Discuss Solutions, Social Affairs Bureau Convened Mediation Yesterday with No Results

Since the British American Tobacco Company announced that the first and second factories in Pudong and the third factory in East Shanghai would all reduce their work to three days a week, it has caused a reaction from the workers, resulting in the closure of the motors. All factories completely stopped working yesterday, and the situation is becoming more and more serious. The Social Affairs Bureau convened mediation in the afternoon, but it was ineffective. Details are recorded below.

All Three Factories Stop Working

The first factory in Lujiazui, Pudong, and the second factory in Lujiazhai have stopped working since the motors were shut down by some workers the day before yesterday afternoon. Workers in all departments did not go to work yesterday. According to the company's announced reduction plan, Monday, Tuesday, and Wednesday are for the tobacco shredding, carpentry, leaf, tobacco cutting, tobacco baking, machinery, stove, and box departments. Tin packing and copper departments are scheduled to work on Wednesday, Thursday, and Friday. Yesterday, except for the tin packing and copper departments, which had about 400 workers working as usual, all other departments, with about 10,000 workers, stopped working. At the same time, the third factory on Taopeng Road in East Shanghai had its iron gate closed, preventing workers from entering the factory. According to the labor side, it is feared that it will be difficult to resume work in the near future.

Labor Side Petitions Party and Government

The Fifth District Cigarette Workers Union believes that the factory suddenly reducing work to three days a week in one month concerns the livelihood of the workers, causing serious disputes. It is urgent to convene a general meeting of all workers to discuss solutions. Therefore, yesterday morning at 10 am, they elected representatives Chen Peide, Liu Dehua, and five others to petition the Municipal Party Department, putting forward two requests: (1) Permission to convene a workers' congress next Tuesday to discuss countermeasures; (2) Requesting the Party and government to order the factory to restore the original state to avoid the expansion of the labor unrest. Zhang Sheng, the director of the Civil Movement Section, received them and approved the request to convene a congress, promising to inform the Public Security Bureau to provide protection. Regarding the request to order the factory to restore the original state, he agreed to handle it together with the Social Affairs Bureau. At the same time, the workers of the third factory in East Shanghai, because the factory closed the iron gate and prevented them from going to work, also sent representatives Lei Qiang, Chen Shikui, and several others to petition the Social Affairs Bureau first. Wang Gang of the Third Section received them and replied that the Social Affairs Bureau had scheduled mediation for this afternoon, hoping that the workers would wait patiently for a solution and not take any drastic action. They then went to the Municipal Party Department to petition, and Lu Yinchu of the Civil Movement Section received them and expressed acceptance of the workers' demands, promising to handle them together with the Social Affairs Bureau. Only then did the workers leave.

Yesterday's Mediation Ineffective

In order to prevent the expansion of the dispute, the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau convened mediation between the two parties at 3 pm yesterday. Chen Peide and Liu Dehua from the labor side, Mr. Lideke (American) from the factory side, translator Chen Xingzhou, and Zhou Lianze from the Municipal Party Department attended. The meeting was chaired by Wang Gang of the Social Affairs Bureau. First, the factory representative reported that the company's sales have been sluggish recently and inventory is piling up. Based on the current sales situation, it is only possible to work two days a week, but in order to take care of the livelihood of the workers, it has been decided to reduce it to three days a week. The labor representative stated that the company has been reducing work to three days in one month, making it difficult for the workers to maintain their livelihoods, and it also violates the labor-capital contract signed in 1928. After repeated persuasion from the Party and government authorities, both parties made concessions, but the labor-capital attitudes remained firm, and it was impossible to resolve the situation. Finally, it was decided that the factory side should submit a written explanation of the reasons for the reduction of work to the bureau for approval this week and then schedule mediation again.

Factory Representative Expresses Responsibility

A reporter from the Ta Kung Pao specifically interviewed Mr. Lideke (transliteration), the personnel director of the company, yesterday. According to him, the factory's business has been affected since the outbreak of the war in North China. Usually, it could ship more than 12,000 boxes a day, but recently sales have suddenly been sluggish and inventory has piled up, so it was necessary to reduce work to three days a week to inject funds. The daily salary of the workers in each factory is about 16,000 yuan. If they work as usual, the wage burden would be heavy, and the amount of goods piled up would be even greater, which would lead to bankruptcy. Therefore, he hoped that the workers would understand the difficulties of the factory and accept this measure.

Shanghai Municipal Council Appoints Committee to Review Milk Disinfection Issues

In order to improve the quality of milk within the concession, the Shanghai Municipal Council, based on the suggestion of the Director of the Health Department, has proposed the establishment of a disinfection plant (Pasteurization Plant) to disinfect Grade B milk (Grade B milk) to reduce the risk of drinking it. After consideration by the Health Committee, the entire committee believes that disinfection is beneficial, but it is more appropriate to allow private operation. It has been decided to appoint a small committee to specifically study this issue. Messrs C. Burgess, A. Hughes, G. H. Wright, and Yuan Ludeng have been appointed as committee members. The scope of work of this investigation committee has also been formulated as follows: (1) To continue the work of the Milk Investigation Committee from 1923 to 1924, studying the cleanliness of milk within the concession; (2) To consider the mandatory disinfection of milk within the concession; (3) Based on the previous article, to consider the most convenient and effective method of disinfecting Grade B milk; (4) To consider the Health Department's central disinfection plant plan, deciding whether it should be run by the council or operated by private companies, subject to considerable restrictions; (5) According to the previous article, to decide whether the disinfection plant should be operated by one company exclusively or divided among several companies; (6) To decide how to manage this disinfection; (7) To investigate the opinions of the dairy farmers, formulating a plan to avoid conflicts with their interests as much as possible; (8) To consider the management methods of transporting milk within the concession and whether to implement regular vaccinations for certain cattle diseases. The above measures have been approved by the Board of Directors on the 11th of this month. Also, during the Health Committee's meeting, the Health Department stated that it does not want to allow milk produced outside the concession to be sold within the concession. If it is smuggled in, it can be prevented, but it believes that it can cooperate with the authorities of the adjacent areas to allow licenses to be mutually recognized and to achieve effective management. In this way, Grade A milk from outside the concession can also be allowed into the concession in the future. Regarding this matter, it has already made informal contact with the authorities of the neighboring areas.

Second Batch of Spring Fish Arrives Yesterday

This Time, the Fish Haul is Abundant

The Wu Song Bao Feng Fish Firm received more than ten boats of second-batch yellow croaker yesterday, including boats named Zuo Zengmao, Guang Zengshun, and Fu Fashun. The Cui Sheng and Shen Tai fish firms also received several boats such as Chen Shunxing and Gao Xiangmao. This time, the fish haul for each boat was quite large, generally over four or five holds, so the market price has slightly decreased. Downriver, each "chou" is sold for thirteen "jin" by market scale, which is equivalent to about eleven "jin" by the old balance scale. Therefore, merchants from various ports, Shanghai merchants, and local households have come to Wu Song to purchase, creating a very crowded scene. The Wu Song market is also more lively than before. According to the boatmen, the second batch of fish appeared on the fifteenth evening of the lunar calendar, and the fish haul was quite abundant. Moreover, the southern tide season came earlier than in previous years, causing all the fishing boats to suffer from having too much fish and not enough salt. In order to preserve high-quality salted fish, they would rather sell the remaining fresh fish at a low price if they ran out of salt. It is said that there are still large fleets of fishing boats scheduled to arrive in Wu Song in the coming days.

Pieces can be picked up one month after payment."

From right to left: Zhu Qiuhen, Gu Meijun, Gu Lanjun, Xuan Jinglin, Ai Xia, Gao Qingping, Hu Ping, Hu Die (Photo by Li Zunyong)

The Invention of the Tonghua Rainproof Textile Factory

Mr. Ni Songsheng, a technician at the Tonghua Rainproof Textile Factory in Huairen Lane, Huining Road, Nanshi, Shanghai, studied in Germany in his earlier years, specializing in dyeing and finishing techniques. After completing his studies, he worked in a factory in Germany, achieving outstanding results. He returned to China two years ago and traveled to various famous regions. He saw that the raincoats sold in the market were all imported goods, causing a loss of several million yuan every year. In contrast, there were no domestic products that could compete with them. Therefore, he devoted himself to research for a long time and finally invented rainproof cloth, rainproof silk, rainproof wool, rainproof serge, etc. All of these are made from domestic cotton, silk, and other textiles, using scientific methods and chemical materials. Not only are the materials of excellent quality, making them suitable for clothing that can be used in both sunny and rainy weather, but they are also washable, durable, and waterproof, without the problems of being airtight or having a sticky odor. The results directly surpass imported products, and the low price is just an added bonus. It is said that all kinds of rainproof textiles have been appraised by important figures in Beijing and Shanghai, and have been praised as unprecedented achievements. Therefore, since the factory opened and set up a distribution center on Penglai Road, Laoximen, only a little over two months have passed. Due to the crowds of customers, wool fabrics are in short supply. It is now expanding greatly and opening night shifts to meet the needs of the Chinese people.

Yesterday morning at around 3:00 am, Shenxin No. 6 Cotton Mill, located at the corner of Hejian Road and Lan Road, Yangshupu, caught fire due to carelessness. Reverend Lei Mingyuan, a Belgian missionary, led more than two hundred and forty missionaries and a large number of aid team members to the frontline war zone to provide on-site aid to wounded soldiers and refugees. This kind of work that brings the dead back to life, along with the provision of medicine, equipment, and labor, is something that all those who embrace humanitarianism cannot help but sympathize with. Elder Ma is making various efforts to provide assistance in Shanghai. This time, Mr. Chen and Mr. Miao also believe that it is their national duty to do everything they can to contribute to this effort, no matter how small. At the same time, Mr. Zhang Taiyan also praised it highly and introduced it, saying, "Miao Zhuancai of Taixian is learned and knowledgeable, and also skilled in writing. He has written explanations for my works such as 'On the Equality of Things,' all of which are the result of more than ten years of effort. He is currently teaching in Xiamen and is willing to sell his articles for the 'Intolerable Society' aid team to contribute to the effort. I also express my deep sympathy."

A Bomb on Rue de Remi

Thrown Into the Tongfeng Cotton Cloth Store

The Tongfengxing Cotton Cloth Store, located at No. 98 Rue de Remi, corner of Avenue Edouard VII in the French Concession, has been open for eight years, specializing in various cotton cloth bolts, with imported goods accounting for more than half of its inventory. The business is quite prosperous. Last night at 7:45 pm, someone suddenly threw a hand-held bomb into the store's front window. It rolled to the left side of the window and did not explode. The bomber took the opportunity to escape, but the incident alarmed nearby shops and pedestrians on the street. In an instant, more than a hundred people stopped to watch. Wang Changsheng, an apprentice at the store, noticed the bomb and reported it to the manager, Xu Mingfu (a 48-year-old from Shaoxing), who in turn reported it to the Macran Police Station on Avenue des Deux Republiques. The police chief immediately ordered Chinese and foreign detectives to rush to the scene to investigate. The bomb was picked up and stored in the police station for further investigation.

Deer Lays an Egg

丨The Materia Medica Calls it "Heart-Protecting Stone," Which Can Treat Heart Pain, Vomiting Blood, and Other Symptoms丨

Mr. Li Shaoguang, a mental physician at No. 656 New Weihaiwei Road in this city, has a deer egg in his collection. It is shaped like a chicken egg, solid on the outside and hollow on the inside, containing very dense strange herbs. The shell is hard and layered, resembling the texture of deer antlers. Its shape is quite peculiar. It is said that his ancestors obtained it from the belly of a deer when they conquered the aborigines. At that time, soldiers who suffered from fever were cured by grinding it with water and drinking it. Afterwards, over the years, the inner strange herbs were revealed. It has been treasured to this day for future use. According to the Compendium of Materia Medica, there is a "Heart-Protecting Stone" that grows in the belly of a deer. The deer eats various detoxification herbs, and its essence accumulates over time and solidifies into a stone, also known as a gemstone. There are two types, one is formed in the deer, and the other is made by Western doctors who collect rare herbs in Lesser Western Countries. Taking it can prevent toxic gases from attacking the heart, hence the name "Heart-Protecting Stone." The method of use is to scrape six grains the size of wheat with a knife, make them into powder, and take them. More can be used without harm, and it will increase energy. Regular use of this medicine will prevent intestinal worms from growing in the abdomen, strengthen the body, and invigorate the spirit. It also treats severe fever and thirst, urinary retention, and diarrhea, all of which are taken with water. For chest injuries and depression without fever, it can be taken with wine or water. If there is fever, it can be taken with half wine and half water. For weakness after illness, it can be taken with half wine and half water. For chest pain, wind-cold qi pain, vomiting roundworms, coughing up blood, and vomiting blood, it can be taken with water. For snake and insect bites, it can be taken with or without wine. For knife and arrow wounds, mad dog bites, and poisonings, apply the powder to the wound, and cover it with cloth to heal it. All of this is seen in the Materia Medica Supplement. It is one of the types of "Heart-Protecting Stone" collected by Mr. Li. This substance was known before the Ming Dynasty, but it is rare in the world. It is specially recorded here for the reference of medical and pharmaceutical professionals.

Madman Randomly Chops People on the Street

Da Chunpu Shot and Killed

Da Yisheng, a 54-year-old Nanjing native, was a small vendor. His wife, Liu, was 54 years old. They had a son named Chunpu, who was 34 years old. The family of three lived together in a small room under an overpass at No. 66 Lane, Huajin Road, due to their poor financial situation. However, Chunpu suffered from mental illness, so he was still unmarried at his age. When his illness flared up on weekdays, he would cry and laugh uncontrollably. Sometimes, he would even drag his parents into the streets and run wildly, or beat them with sticks. Although Da was disturbed by this, he could not bear to abandon his son due to their father-son relationship, so he still kept him at home. Unexpectedly, yesterday afternoon at around 3:00 pm, Chunpu's mental illness flared up again. He suddenly took a kitchen knife from his home and wielded it wildly in the street, chopping at anyone he encountered. At that time, passersby scattered and fled in all directions. When Chunpu reached the entrance of Huajin Road, Lou Xiru, a 42-year-old Ningbo native, happened to be there. He lived at No. 9, Huaixian Lane, Xueyuan Road, and was a salesman at the Yixing Company on Ermalu. He was coming out of his house on business when he passed by the area. Chunpu took advantage of his unpreparedness, caught up from behind, and raised the kitchen knife to chop at Lou's neck. Lou noticed it, but it was too late to avoid it, so he was chopped on the neck with a knife, about four inches long and several points deep. Blood flowed like a torrent. Lou turned around to look and saw that the person wielding the knife was a madman. Knowing that there was no point in reasoning with him, he immediately hired a rickshaw and went to the Shanghai Hospital for treatment. It is said that his injuries are very serious. However, after Chunpu chopped at Lou, he continued to wield the kitchen knife and headed straight for Hongqiao. A large crowd followed him, but no one dared to step forward to catch him. Wu Linqing, a police officer on duty at the nearby No. 32 post, noticed him and knew that he would cause trouble, so he quickly stepped forward and ordered him to stop, intending to arrest him. Unexpectedly, Chunpu was not afraid when he saw the police arrive. Instead, he raised the knife and chopped at Officer Wu's left hand. Officer Wu could not avoid it and was chopped on his left hand, immediately injuring the web of his hand and causing it to bleed. Seeing that he was so reckless, Officer Wu had no choice but to pull out his pistol and fire a shot at the ground. At this time, Chunpu had only walked a few steps and stumbled and fell to the ground due to his hasty steps. As a result, the bullet fired by Officer Wu accidentally hit Chunpu's chest. However, Chunpu still tried to struggle to get up after being injured. Officer Wu took the opportunity to bravely rush forward while injured, snatch the kitchen knife, and finally capture him. After taking him back to the No. 2 Precinct of the First District, Chunpu was exhausted, pale, and short of breath. The precinct sent police to take him to the Shanghai Hospital for treatment, but he died before he could be treated after arriving at the hospital.

International Trade Bureau Convenes Tea Merchants to Discuss Relief

Improving Tea Production Methods, Implementing Rural Inspections, Telegram to Finance Minister Song Requesting Countries to Reduce Tax Rates, Requesting Shanghai Banks and Money Shops to Relieve Russian Tea Sales

The International Trade Bureau of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, due to the disastrous decline in the tea market, urgently needs to find ways to remedy the situation. Therefore, yesterday afternoon at 3:00 pm, it convened the City Tea Industry Association, Huacha Company, and various tea merchants at the bureau's conference room to discuss relief measures. The details of the meeting are recorded below:

Attending Representatives

The attending representatives included Guo Weibai, Director of General Affairs of the International Trade Bureau, Ji Zejin, Director of the Guidance Department and Secretary, Zhang Pansun, Chen Yizhou, Peng Zhiping, Zhuo Huapu, Sun Zishou, Hu Dexin, representatives of the Tea Industry Association, Hong Mengpan, representative of Jin Jianxing Company, Chen Bingwen, Chen Xiaowen, representative of Fan Baosheng Company, Wang Yinting, representative of Wang Yutai Company, and more than ten other people.

Discussion of Measures

After the meeting began, Chairman Guo Weibai reported on the purpose of the meeting and briefly described the opinions of Tao Yin, the Deputy Consul of China in Liverpool, to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs on improving tea and promoting international trade. Then, Ji Zejin proposed several relief measures for open discussion. Each representative expressed their opinions. The final decisions were: (1) Improvement of tea exports: (A) How to make the tea taste stronger to suit the British preference. The rural economy of our country is declining, and old tea trees are planted and old tea production methods are used, in the hope of taking shortcuts, resulting in a decline in sales. Now, we should focus on increasing fertilizer and cultivation. (B) How to make the selling price lower to compete with Indian, Ceylonese, and Japanese tea. Samples of various teas should be sent to our country's consuls in various countries, especially focusing on the United Kingdom, the United States, and Russia, to widely promote them. The consuls should also investigate the names and locations of companies that purchase Chinese tea so that they can trade directly without going through foreign merchants, so as to reduce costs and expand sales channels. (C) Regarding foreign tariffs on Chinese tea, Finance Minister Song Ziwen should be telegraphed to pay attention to this matter and try to reduce tariffs when attending the London Economic Conference. (D) Regarding whether advertising or replanting with Indian or Ceylonese tea would be effective, this matter is difficult to implement. Rural inspections must be carried out first to find ways to improve. (2) Regarding the sale of tea to Russia: (A) The City Foreign Firm Tea Industry Association has submitted a request to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to forward it to the Ministry of Finance for relief. The Ministry of Finance has instructed the Shanghai banks and money shops to provide relief. We must consult with them again. (B) The establishment of a special bureau for trade with Russia has been discussed between Minister of Industry and Commerce Chen Gongbo and Soviet Ambassador Bogomolov in Beijing. The Russian ambassador expressed his support. Today, the Russian state-owned TASS news agency has raised objections, saying that our country has not established special bureaus for trade with Japan and the United Kingdom, but only with Russia, which is considered unequal. This still needs to be discussed further.

Petition for Relief

The original document from Chen Zhaoshou, Chairman of the Shanghai Foreign Firms Tea Trade Association, and other committee members, to the Ministry of Industry, is hereby recorded below: Petitioning for special relief due to the extreme decline of exported boxed tea. It is humbly submitted that the export of black and green boxed tea has historically been handled by foreign merchants to Europe and America, with Russian merchants being particularly significant buyers, accounting for as much as half of the entire trade at its peak. Since the 18th year (of the Republic), the amount has decreased year by year, and in the 21st year, Russian merchants reduced their purchases drastically, almost to zero, with a total purchase of only over 30,000 boxes for the whole year, valued at less than 600,000. Purchases of tea dust, old tea, and compressed tea bricks from Hankou for export were also no more than 300 taels. The reasons for this are attributed to competition and encroachment from India, Ceylon, Java, and Japan, as well as the economic policies of those countries, which restrict tea consumption. However, the biggest reason is that Russian merchants are assisting foreign firms in purchasing tea from India, Ceylon, Java, and Japan, with payment terms of twelve months from the date of shipment, while purchases in China require immediate cash payment. Therefore, they abandon China for these other countries. Chinese tea merchants are weak and unable to compete with foreign tea. Zhaoshou sought an audience with the Vice President of the Central Bank, who advised him to detail the plight to the Ministry for thorough investigation of the current procedures for Russian merchants purchasing foreign tea and to seek relief. Therefore, without fear of being presumptuous, we present a detailed account of the entire situation, appealing for extraordinary support so that natural domestic products do not disappear from foreign markets. It is estimated that the decline in trade in both Shanghai and Hankou totals four to five million taels annually, causing widespread distress. We humbly request that Your Excellency forward this information to Minister of Finance Song, requesting that a syndicate be designated to lend large sums to Russian merchants specifically for purchasing Chinese tea, which would alleviate this crisis. We beg that a method be devised, and that the Russian merchants be invited to discuss the matter, as rescuing the nation and aiding businesses rests on this single action. Respectfully submitted to Minister Chen of the Ministry of Industry.

Robbery News via Telephone

Chen Wanyou Upheld the Meaning of Mutual Assistance by Disregarding Danger and Personally Investigating at a Neighbor's Home

丨Detectives Arrived, but the Robbers Were Gone, Only Apprehending One Lookout丨

In the Anqing Lane of the Moore Road area in western Shanghai, there were five houses, among which No. 142 was the residence of Hou Anzhou, a rickshaw puller. Adjacent to No. 141 was Chen Wanyou's paint business. Hou's family was quite wealthy, attracting the attention of bandits. At 6:30 AM the previous morning, six robbers formed a gang and secretly went to commit robbery. After reaching Anqing Lane, one robber was assigned to loiter at the lane entrance as a lookout. The five robbers entered the lane and knocked on Hou's front door. At that time, Chen Wanyou's rickshaw puller, Li Asan, was squatting at Chen's doorstep washing clothes. He suddenly saw a stranger and was suspicious. Then, Hou's double doors creaked open, and the five robbers swarmed in, forcibly dragging the person who opened the door inside. The door was then closed tightly. Li became even more suspicious and quickly informed Chen Wanyou of the situation. Chen had known Hou for a long time and, suspecting that these unexpected visitors might be robbers, decided not to stand idly by. He tried to call Hou Anzhou on the phone, but the five robbers had already begun the robbery. Three robbers with handguns went upstairs to search for valuables, while the other two robbers were downstairs to prevent the occupants from raising an alarm. Hou heard the phone ringing and picked up the receiver. As soon as he began to speak, the robbers snatched the phone away. Chen Wanyou was unaware that Hou had been prevented from speaking, so he kept listening on the phone. Although Hou was unable to speak directly to Chen, the broken words he spoke to the robbers, "My family has no money; even if we did, it would be in the bank. Why have you come to demand it?" were all transmitted to Chen's ear through the phone. Chen then knew for certain that Hou's house had been robbed. He immediately reported the situation to the Jing'an Temple Police Station via telephone, requesting that detectives be dispatched quickly. He wanted to determine the truth of the robbery, disregarding the danger, he personally went to Hou's house to investigate. Before leaving, he told his rickshaw puller, Li Asan, "If I go to Hou's house and don't come out immediately, then there must be robbers in his house. I will surely be monitored by the robbers. You must quickly urge the police station to send detectives." After speaking, he went to knock on Hou's door. The robbers inside heard the knocking, opened the door, and immediately dragged Chen inside. Li saw that his master had indeed fallen into danger and shouted Chen's name wildly. The robbers in the house recognized the voice as belonging to their lookout accomplice and, thinking that the matter had been exposed, abandoned their search of boxes and chests. They only grabbed the stolen clothes, jewelry, and cash and rushed out of the door, fleeing out of the lane. When the police detectives arrived in cars, all five robbers had already disappeared. Only the Anhui-native robber Xi Shaoting, who was acting as a lookout at the entrance of the lane, was still loitering and was arrested. They then entered Hou's house to inquire about the circumstances of the robbery. Hou and Chen briefly recounted the events. Chen also said that after he entered the house, the silver dollars in his pocket, totaling one dollar and eighty cents, were also stolen. Hou estimated the loss to be over 950 yuan, and a list was given to the detectives, along with Xi, to be taken back to the police station. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the First Special District Court, where Judge Wu Tingqi conducted a preliminary hearing. Police lawyer Li Zhishan requested that the robber Xi be interrogated and then detained for further investigation. Detectives Wu Zhiyun, Ma Derong, Guan Huchen, and others reported the process of apprehending Xi. Xi Shaoting claimed that he was passing by and went into the lane to buy a pancake when he was arrested. However, witnesses such as Li Asan testified that Xi was indeed a lookout robber, and there were no pancake vendors in the lane. Judge Wu then ordered Xi Shaoting to be remanded in custody, with a new hearing scheduled in seven days for further investigation.

Large Bomb Excavated from Tanzigang, Weighing Approximately 300 Pounds

Tanzigang in Zhabei had been silted up for a long time, making navigation difficult. Therefore, local gentry and merchants recently hired workers to dredge it. Yesterday at around 10:00 AM, the river workers were excavating the soil when they suddenly discovered a large black bomb. They immediately found a way to lift it out. It was shaped like an olive with a flat bottom, and at the bottom was an iron ring, with a diameter of about one foot. It weighed approximately 300 pounds. At the same time, a large cannonball, weighing more than ten pounds, was also excavated. Guo Shunji, a local merchant, concerned about the safety of the river workers, had them send it to the second team of the Pengpu Security Corps, who then forwarded it to the Fourth District Public Security Bureau for disposal.

Deceptive Acts by the Japanese

Selling Flour as Tooth-Setting Powder and Taking the Opportunity to Steal Over 400 Yuan: Zhang Yingming Was Fooled and Is Now Suspected

Zhang Yingming, an elderly man from Ningbo, has been running the Yingming tooth-setting shop at the mouth of Tangjia Lane on North Zhejiang Road near the Old Garbage Bridge for many years. Recently, Zhang was introduced to a Japanese ronin living in Shanghai by Li Yutang, and they became quite close. What kind of business they were engaged in, outsiders could not know. The day before yesterday, at 4:00 PM, four Japanese and two Chinese people came to Zhang's shop. They gave him several paper packages. Zhang took one package outside, and the rest were hidden upstairs by his family. The Japanese and Chinese people initially stayed in the shop to wait for Zhang, but later left on their own. At 8:00 PM that evening, Zhang suddenly sent Li Yutang to report to the Hongkou Police Station, saying that after he left the shop, these people went to the kitchen, took a knife, destroyed his iron box, and stole 420 yuan. Later, he learned of this upon his return, and went to No. 10 Jiuyu Lane on Yalu Road to look for the Japanese man he knew, but was unable to find him. Therefore, he specially reported the incident for investigation. However, at the time, Zhang's concubine, Zhang Zhou, had detained one of the two Chinese people, but then released him. The police chief, knowing that Zhang's shop was under the jurisdiction of the Mixed Court Police Station, transferred the case to Detective Tao Afu of the Mixed Court Police Station, who went to Zhang's shop for questioning. He suspected that Zhang might be colluding with the Japanese in illegal trade. He searched the shop and found five packages of a substance resembling morphine upstairs, weighing eight and a half pounds. He then took Zhang, his concubine Zhang Zhou, and Li Yutang to the police station. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the First Special District Court, where Judge Wu Tingqi conducted a preliminary hearing. Police lawyer Li Zhishan stated the circumstances of Zhang's and Li's report to the police and the detectives' investigation. Because it was still necessary to test whether the seized substance was morphine, he requested a postponement. Zhang then testified that the Japanese man was introduced to him by Li. He had asked about the powder used for tooth-setting, saying that he was also in the business. Yesterday, he brought several packages of powder to sell to him. Because he did not know the quality of the substance, he took a package to the Caishi Road in the French Concession to ask a colleague to examine it. He did not expect that it would turn out to be flour disguised as powder. When he returned and learned of the incident, he went to find the Japanese man to negotiate, but could not find him. Therefore, he reported the incident to the police. The seized substance belonged to the Japanese man and could be tested. If it turned out to be morphine, he would willingly admit his guilt. Lawyer Li said that according to Zhang's testimony, it seemed that he was also being fooled by someone. He requested bail, and the police did not object. Judge Wu then ordered Zhang Yingming and Zhang Zhou to be released on bail, while Li Yutang was remanded in custody pending the results of the testing.

Shared by Over Twenty People: The Elderly Given Funds to Remarry, the Youngest Only Sixteen Years Old, Everyone Benefited

Major Search in Baoyuli

Due to Anonymous Letters, Forty to Fifty People Were Detained

The Dazimingzhong Police Station in the French Concession has recently received more than ten anonymous letters. The content of the letters mainly stated that there were kidnapping organizations in Baoyuli, as well as opium dens and gambling dens, and that thieves were hiding in hotels and inns. Therefore, the police chief acted discreetly and dispatched additional Chinese and French detectives on regular duty, as well as a large number of Vietnamese, Russian, and Chinese police, totaling over a hundred people, to tightly surround the entrances of each lane in Baoyuli. Yesterday (12th) morning at 6:00 AM, the Chinese and French detectives searched each household. All the shops along the roads, such as Caishi Street along the south of Baoyuli, Avenue Edward VII along the north, and Dongxinqiao Street along the east, as well as the residents in the lane, totaling over a hundred houses, were all searched. The search lasted for two hours. During the search, pedestrians in the lane were not allowed to enter or exit. The search ended at around 8:00 AM. As a result, over fifty or sixty opium pipes, opium dross, small bore guns, and various opium paraphernalia, opium paste, opium ashes, and red pills were seized. The most red pills and opium pipes were found in the Anle No. 2 Inn. Suspected thieves and opium gamblers, totaling forty to fifty people, were arrested, fully loaded into two trucks, and taken to the police station to report to the police chief for further investigation. During the search, most of the residents were fast asleep and were awakened from their dreams. At that time, vegetables were being sold on Caishi Street, and a large number of armed police surrounded Baoyuli on three sides, not allowing pedestrians to enter or exit. The situation was quite serious. When the search was completed, the detectives withdrew their forces, and Caishi Street returned to its original state.

Letter

To the esteemed editors: We have recently read in your newspaper an article about a prisoner filing a petition with the Ministry of Justice requesting a thorough investigation of the Caohejing Prison. The rights and wrongs of the matter will be judged fairly. In addition to telegraphing the Judicial Administration Department and the Jiangsu Higher Court to send personnel for thorough investigation, we are corresponding with your newspaper's reporter and colleagues in the press to visit the prison together to clarify the truth. We hope that you will publish the original letter in advance. Respectfully, Tian Jinghua, Warden of Jiangsu Second Prison, Shanghai Shenbao, May 12th.

Mr. Li Gongpu's Speech on National Humiliation Week: My Views on the Future of Sino-Japanese Relations

May 9th at the YMCA

Friends, the topic I am going to discuss today is my view on the future of Sino-Japanese relations. We know that the relationship between China and Japan did not start today. It has a long history dating back to the 21st year of the Guangxu reign. We remember what Mr. Cai Zimin said the day before yesterday in his speech "Japan's Policy Toward China"—he mentioned that from Japan's annexation of Taiwan and occupation of Korea to its current further creation of puppet states, it is still the old trick of annexing Korea. However, before the "May Fourth Movement," everyone felt a sense of national doom. After the "May Fourth Movement" until the "September 18th Incident," this fear seemed to have diminished, because this is a natural phenomenon of the Chinese people being bound by deeply rooted autocratic systems, intellectual traditions, and family concepts. Although the people's spirit after the "May Fourth Movement" had changed somewhat, it was revitalized during the September 18th Incident. Everyone thought that imperialists did not benefit much from having colonies. In the trend of the times, it was believed that imperialists only wanted economic aggression and not territorial aggression. Of course, the ignorant and uneducated would not understand this, and even the educated were infected by laziness and became lost in a dream. When the September 18th Incident occurred the year before last, most people still did not think that it was a fundamental issue of national survival, but rather that Zhang Xueliang had messed it up. The reason for these views was that everyone had not suffered deeply before the January 28th Incident, so after the January 28th Incident and before the loss of Rehe, the people were unusually decadent. After the loss of Rehe, when the Japanese army captured Shanhaiguan, attacked Qinhuangdao, and approached Beiping and Tianjin, the crisis increased daily. Only then did people realize that the past so-called imperialism was not territorial aggression, and that the various complacent and erroneous psychologies that China would not perish were proven wrong. Now, let's explain the situation from three aspects: Japan's situation, the international situation, and China's current situation. Then we can infer the future of Sino-Japanese relations.

Japan's situation can also be analyzed from three points: 1. Politics: After Japan's military success, it continued with active construction, such as governing Korea and Taiwan very well with decisive force after occupying them, so as to compensate for the losses during the war. From Japan's point of view, it is definitely an undeniable fact that governing the Northeast well recently is beneficial to itself. Also, Japan is a country with mixed ideologies, especially narrow nationalism. Tanaka's policies and the people's fanaticism all support the realization of imperialism, which can enrich military, popular, and political power. 2. Economy: Chinese scholars often like to point out the danger of Japan's economic crisis, but it should be known that Japan's economic crisis was not caused by the invasion of China. For example, the United States is the richest country, yet it still experienced an economic crisis, and at the same time, countries such as Britain and France were affected by it, so Japan's economic crisis is also global. Although its market will inevitably suffer losses after a war, it can immediately restore the market by conquering a piece of land and compensate for the losses of the war. If Japan occupies the Northeast, everything can be better than under Zhang Xueliang. The public sale of opium can eliminate exploitation. In the past, opium was expensive, but now it is cheap. As for whether it is good or bad for everyone after consuming it, that is another question. The purpose is only to gain the trust of Chinese capitalists, and at the same time, raw materials can also be increased. Wherever it gets, it gets the products of that place. Although I have not seen the Northeast with my own eyes, I can know from the contents of the "Manchukuo Yearbook" recently published by the Japanese for the puppet state that the Japanese have been able to achieve the benefits of economic recovery by organizing mineral production, railways, and other things. This is one example. 3. "National Defense": Japan's national defense can be divided into internal and external aspects. Internally, if there is an attack from the air, can it be defended against? During the European War, London was threatened and bombed by German aircraft and felt panicked. The power of the air force now is more advanced than during the European War, so Japan's national defense can never be completely safe, because who dares to say that they have adequate defenses against aviation? Therefore, to keep the sea defense from Tokyo to Korea, it is necessary to expand the land. Externally, if a protracted war is to be fought, materials must be enriched. However, Japan is not enough, and neither is Korea, so it must expand its land to enrich its materials. In summary, Japan has the necessity to invade land.

In the international arena, the relationship of various countries with China is different from that of Japan. In the international arena, China is a part of the aggression, while for Japan, China is the only target of aggression that is most closely related. Such means of violent aggression and bullying of small and weak nations were the usual tricks of past imperialists, so this time, the international community will not be able to use justice to restrain Japan except by stopping it with force, because Japan can use the fact that various countries are also invading China as an excuse. Recently, judging from the public opinion of various countries, Japanese publications have expressed the affection of the United States for Japan and said that no one in the United States opposes Japan's economic aggression in Manchuria and Mongolia. They also quoted the words of Wilson, the head of the National YMCA, the Secretary of War under President Wilson, and the leader of the Civil Rights Party, Newton Baker, expressing sympathy for Japan's small land area and large population. Although some people say that the Japanese words cannot be trusted, the fact that Japan has a small land area and a large population is well known to the powers and is something we should know. At the Pacific Conference, Japan always mentions the population problem, because at least this way it can gain the sympathy of the world. The other day, a Reuters dispatch from London reported that Professor R. H. Tawney, an economic historian at the University of London, said in a speech at a certain school: "China should immediately rise up and take action, otherwise foreign aggression will take its place. China's chaos has lasted for 30 years and has not stopped, which is really pessimistic. When he was in China, Shenyang had already been lost, and the Chinese people only expressed anger and did not take any action, which really showed the patience of the Chinese people. If the League of Nations had taken decisive action earlier, Japan would not have dared to seize all of Manchuria." The above shows a glimpse of the international attitude towards China and Japan. Therefore, since the Sino-Japanese incident occurred, the simultaneous resignation of the three Chinese ministers is a clear point.

Regarding China, Mr. Zhang Yousan said the other day that there are five ways: fighting, negotiating peace, resisting, relying [on others], and delaying. Except for the last one, which is not a way at all, but are the previous ones really ways? Think about it: if you can't fight, then fighting is not a way; if you can't negotiate peace, then negotiating peace is certainly not a way. Where is there a real way in all of this? Regarding the recent battle against Japan along the Great Wall after the loss of Rehe, the knowledgeable are indifferent to this national war. As for those who can help the soldiers and care about them, they are mostly hardworking farmers. Furthermore, when the Japanese diplomat Yosuke Matsuoka returned home and was enthusiastically welcomed by many people, he severely criticized his countrymen, saying that a large portion of them did not know how dangerous the situation the country was in. We see that Japanese diplomats encourage the people in this way, but how many people in China are willing to point out mistakes? There is no overall plan, nor is there a unanimous expression from the government and the public. Some people say that the people have not yet awakened, but if the people do not rise up to save themselves now, it will be difficult to save the country when it is lost in the future. In the Korean restoration movement, there is a story that can serve as a warning to us. When it started in 1919, the European War had ended, and various countries were holding a peace conference in Paris. The Koreans thought that the time had come. In the first month of that year, the national Bible study meeting was held as usual. Pastor Kim Pil-mo used the name of selling church newspapers to travel around the churches and secretly contacted the leaders, and agreed to hold a demonstration at 2:00 pm on March 2nd, because March 3rd was the funeral day of King Lee Tae of Korea. People from all provinces and counties gathered to attend the funeral, intending to take the opportunity to arouse the national spirit of shared hatred. At that time, Korea also had the so-called Cheondoist religion, whose leader, Son Dong-hee, had the ambition to restore the country. His followers exceeded one million. He joined forces with Kim Pil-mo to start the uprising. The schools in the church and the schools outside the church first united, pre-printed flyers, and widely prepared national flags. On March 2nd, the leaders of various churches specially held a citizens' meeting at Taehwagwan in Seoul, with tens of thousands of people attending. They raised the Taegeuk national flag and held a cordial ceremony. The leaders gave heartfelt speeches and immediately wrote to the Governor-General of Korea, Hasegawa Yoshimichi, saying, "Our sacred Korean people advocate freedom and independence in this enlightened era. From now on, you can quickly return to your country and do not hurt the harmony of the people of the two countries." The Governor-General was shocked and immediately imposed martial law as if facing a formidable enemy, dispatching dozens of cars and armed forces to arrest the leaders. The leaders were kind and friendly, and shouted, "We have not finished speaking yet, please wait a moment," and continued to speak calmly, distributing flyers to the masses, saluting the national flag, and shouting "Long live independence" three times, and then calmly went to be arrested, a total of 33 people. Jesus pastor, Gu Seon-ju, Choi Seong-mo, Cheondoist leader Son Byeong-hee, Oh Se-chang, and Yang Han-muk were among the most famous. The Japanese thought that nothing would happen after capturing the leaders, but unexpectedly, three days later, the whole of Korea was shaken. Every household had the Taegeuk national flag, and everyone shouted "Long live independence." Demonstrations spread throughout the 13 provinces and more than 360 counties. Children and women also marched in teams, shouting "Return our mountains and rivers, national self-determination." Arrests and executions followed one after another. First, Kim Gyu-sik, a plenipotentiary representative, was sent to the Paris Peace Conference to petition. On April 12, with the approval of the four countries, he submitted a petition for independence. Overseas Chinese sent letters and telegrams everywhere to seek assistance. On April 17, a provisional government was organized, with members including Syngman Rhee, Kim Gyu-sik, An Chang-ho, Yi Dong-hwi, Choi Jae-hyeong, Mun Chang-beom, Yi Si-yeong, and Yi Dong-nyeong. On May 12, the United States recognized Syngman Rhee as the ambassador to the United States and allowed the Independence Hall in Washington to host him. The Japanese saw that the situation was getting worse and worse and extremely dangerous, so they mobilized the military and police to carry out massacres, roasting people naked, nailing their feet, dissecting their bellies, burying three or five people alive, or destroying entire villages. From March to June, about 30,000 people were brutally killed, more than 2,000 women, and more than 10,000 people were imprisoned. Let us think about it. Under the strict surveillance of the Japanese, the national spirit of struggle that was created with one or twenty years of effort can make tens of thousands of men, women, old and young compatriots disregard life and death and fight for the survival of the motherland. How great is this spirit? However, once it is suppressed by supreme violence, it is almost completely wiped out in two or three months. From this point of view, we know how difficult and arduous the restoration after national subjugation is!

Based on the above analysis and personal observation, I speculate that the future of Sino-Japanese relations will be no more than two possibilities: (1) International co-management. Some people think that international co-management will cause a second world war, but that is not the case, because international co-management is not all the powers gathering together, opening the map of China, and dividing it carefully. Instead, before the Second World War, the powers must find ways to avoid a world war. On the surface, they still maintain a peaceful attitude, but in reality, they go a step further than now, using internal wars, with an imperialist power behind each warlord, to create a country that is seemingly divided but not divided, seemingly unified but not unified.

(2) National self-awakening and self-salvation, and cooperation with the government. What the government dares not do is the government's lack of power, which is also the people's lack of power. Let me give you an example. For example, "peace" should be negotiated after the fall of Shenyang and before the loss of Jinzhou, but who would dare to say this at that time? If such a powerful person came out at that time to advocate it and the government did not listen, I am afraid that the government would have been overthrown long ago. It is the same now. For example, some people say that this is what the government does not allow, not that the people have no power. Then let me ask, are "bandits" allowed by the government? You must know that if the people know how to save themselves and rise up automatically, then the government cannot interfere. During the "January 28th Incident" last year, the Shanghai people enthusiastically helped the 19th Route Army. Was this instigated by the government? Therefore, the people should cultivate and train their own strength to supervise the government, because maintaining social order is the government's intention, but we cannot expect the current government to deal with Japan in a strong manner. If we people feel that the fire is already burning our eyebrows, we should fight Japan at all costs. Then the people of all provinces and regions should automatically rise up to urge the government to resist Japan. For example, when Roosevelt was appointed during this economic crisis, Congress unprecedentedly granted the president many special powers, but when it came to solving the war debt problem, many leaders came out to express their opposition to extending the debt. This opinion made Roosevelt have to be wary of the war debt issue. You must know that looking at China's political history, it has been deeply inertial, and there is no resistance to foreign aggression. Moreover, China is an agricultural economic self-sufficient country, which is far from being able to compete with scientific and industrial countries. However, the Chinese national character inherently contains the characteristics of courage, simplicity, hard work, and endurance to extreme oppression. If it can be closely united, it will surely be able to forge its own way out of difficult circumstances. Therefore, the last hope is that the people of all regions cultivate strength, train their own spirit, organize groups, and cooperate with the government. If this step can be achieved, then any government that is not right can be overthrown. If the people do not know how to save themselves, they will surely be eliminated. Do not blame the government alone. We must recognize that cultivation, training, and organization are the only work we should do. (Recorded by Xu Zhi)

Jiangsu Education Fees to Be Issued for One Month Before the Summer Festival

When the Jiangsu Education Funding Management Office held a meeting of auditors on the afternoon of the 10th, it reported that the current treasury balance was over 120,000 yuan. Previously issued payment notices that had not yet been cashed amounted to over 190,000 yuan. After offsetting income and expenses, there was still a shortage of over 70,000 yuan. They are now urging various counties to remit education fees in order to clear the already issued payment notices. As the Summer Festival is approaching and various schools need funds urgently, the auditors approved the issuance of payment notices for the full month of February (with rural teachers and experimental primary schools continuing to follow the usual practice). These notices will be issued before the 20th of this month, and schools will receive the funds before the 25th to meet the expenses of the Summer Festival.

Ministry of Education Explains the Supplementary Examination Issue After the Graduation Examination

▲Instruction to the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education

The Ministry of Education, in response to the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education's request for clarification on three points regarding supplementary examinations for senior high school general studies students after the graduation examination, specifically instructed the bureau as follows: "Received and understood. Students who participate in the secondary school student graduation examination retest and still fail in one or two subjects should comply with Article 9 of the Provisional Regulations for Secondary and Primary School Student Graduation Examinations and study for an additional year. Remedial studies can be done in or outside the school. If the distance between the current examination and the next is only one semester, the remedial period for these students is allowed to be shortened to one semester. Senior high school students without graduation qualifications may not apply to universities. Students who fail the retest have not obtained senior high school graduation qualifications and are not allowed to apply to universities. The secondary and primary school graduation examination is to determine the graduation grades of secondary and primary school students and promote the efficiency of secondary and primary school education, and is not an entrance examination. Therefore, senior high school graduates with excellent graduation examination results may not be exempt from the university entrance examination. Scholarship amounts are a kind of reward and relief method for schools to students who have excellent academic performance or poor family backgrounds, and have nothing to do with the graduation examination. Therefore, scholarships cannot be given due to excellent graduation examination results. Please comply accordingly."

Jinling Women's University Patriotic Fundraising Carnival

The students of Nanjing Jinling Women's University are known for their enthusiasm for national salvation work and are the crown of the women's world. They have rushed to make thousands of clothes, trousers, and wound dressings for the front lines, sparing no effort. After class, they often train in first aid work or go to neighboring communities to spread the word about the national crisis.
